 CHAPTER IV 

 an elephant hunt 

 now I do not propose to narrate at full length all the incident of our 
 long travel up to Sitanda 's Kraal , near the junction of the Lukanga and 
 Kalukwe Rivers . it be a journey of more than a thousand mile from 
 Durban , the last three hundred or so of which we have to make on foot , 
 owe to the frequent presence of the dreadful " tsetse " fly , whose bite 
 be fatal to all animal except donkey and man . 

 we leave Durban at the end of January , and it be in the second week of 
 May that we camp near Sitanda 's Kraal . our adventure on the way be 
 many and various , but as they be of the sort which befall every 
 african hunter - with one exception to be presently detailed - I shall 
 not set they down here , lest I should render this history too wearisome . 

 at Inyati , the outlying trading station in the Matabele country , of 
 which Lobengula   a great and cruel scoundrel   be king , with many 
 regret we part from our comfortable wagon . only twelve oxen remain 
 to we out of the beautiful span of twenty which I have buy at Durban . 
 one we lose from the bite of a cobra , three have perish from " poverty " 
 and the want of water , one stray , and the other three die from 
 eat the poisonous herb call " tulip . " five more sickened from this 
 cause , but we manage to cure they with dos of an infusion make by 
 boil down the tulip leave . if administer in time this be a very 
 effective antidote . 

 the wagon and the oxen we leave in the immediate charge of Goza and Tom , 
 our driver and leader , both trustworthy boy , request a worthy 
 Scotch missionary who live in this distant place to keep an eye on 
 they . then , accompany by Umbopa , Khiva , Ventv"gel , and half a dozen 
 bearer whom we hire on the spot , we start off on foot upon our wild 
 quest . I remember we be all a little silent on the occasion of this 
 departure , and I think that each of we be wonder if we should ever 
 see our wagon again ; for my part I never expect to do so . for a while 
 we tramp on in silence , till Umbopa , who be march in front , break 
 into a Zulu chant about how some brave man , tired of life and the 
 tameness of thing , start off into a vast wilderness to find new 
 thing or die , and how , lo and behold ! when they have travel far into 
 the wilderness they find that it be not a wilderness at all , but a 
 beautiful place full of young wife and fat cattle , of game to hunt and 
 enemy to kill . 

 then we all laugh and take it for a good oman . Umbopa be a cheerful 
 savage , in a dignified sort of way , when he be not suffer from one 
 of his fit of brooding , and he have a wonderful knack of keep up our 
 spirit . we all grow very fond of he . 

 and now for the one adventure to which I be go to treat myself , for 
 I do dearly love a hunting yarn . 

 about a fortnight 's march from Inyati we come across a peculiarly 
 beautiful bit of well - water woodland country . the kloof in the hill 
 be cover with dense bush , " idoro " bush as the native call it , and 
 in some place , with the " wacht - een - beche , " or " wait - a - little thorn , " 
 and there be great quantity of the lovely " machabell " tree , laden 
 with refresh yellow fruit have enormous stone . this tree be the 
 elephant 's favourite food , and there be not want sign that the 
 great brute have be about , for not only be their spoor frequent , but 
 in many place the tree be break down and even uproot . the 
 elephant be a destructive feeder . 

 one evening , after a long day 's march , we come to a spot of great 
 loveliness . at the foot of a bush - clothe hill lie a dry river - bed , in 
 which , however , be to be find pool of crystal water all trodden 
 round with the hoof - print of game . face this hill be a park - like 
 plain , where grow clump of flat - top mimosa , vary with occasional 
 glossy - leave machabell , and all round stretch the sea of pathless , 
 silent bush . 

 as we emerge into this river - bed path suddenly we start a troop of 
 tall giraffe , who gallop , or rather sail off , in their strange 
 gait , their tail screw up over their back , and their hoof rattle 
 like castanet . they be about three hundred yard from we , and 
 therefore practically out of shot , but Good , who be walk ahead , and 
 who have an express load with solid ball in his hand , could not resist 
 temptation . lift his gun , he let drive at the last , a young cow . by 
 some extraordinary chance the ball strike it full on the back of the 
 neck , shatter the spinal column , and that giraffe go rolling head 
 over heel just like a rabbit . I never see a more curious thing . 

 " curse it ! " say Good - for I be sorry to say he have a habit of use 
 strong language when excite - contract , no doubt , in the course of 
 his nautical career ; " curse it ! I have   kill he . " 

 " Ou , Bougwan , " ejaculate the Kafirs ; " ou ! ou ! " 

 they call Good " Bougwan , " or Glass Eye , because of his eye - glass . 

 " oh , ' Bougwan ! ' " re - echo Sir Henry and I , and from that day Good 's 
 reputation as a marvellous shot be establish , at any rate among the 
 Kafirs . really he be a bad one , but whenever he miss we overlook 
 it for the sake of that giraffe . 

 have set some of the " boy " to cut off the good of the giraffe 's 
 meat , we go to work to build a ' scherm " near one of the pool and 
 about a hundred yard to its right . this be do by cut a quantity 
 of thorn bush and pile they in the shape of a circular hedge . then 
 the space enclose be smooth , and dry tambouki grass , if obtainable , 
 be make into a bed in the centre , and a fire or fire light . 

 by the time the ' scherm " be finish the moon peep up , and our 
 dinner of giraffe steak and roasted marrow - bone be ready . how we 
 enjoy those marrow - bone , though it be rather a job to crack they ! I 
 know of no great luxury than giraffe marrow , unless it be elephant 's 
 heart , and we have that on the morrow . we eat our simple meal by the 
 light of the moon , pause at time to thank Good for his wonderful 
 shot ; then we begin to smoke and yarn , and a curious picture we must 
 have make squat there round the fire . I , with my short grizzle 
 hair stick up straight , and Sir Henry with his yellow lock , which 
 be get rather long , be rather a contrast , especially as I be 
 thin , and short , and dark , weigh only nine stone and a half , and Sir 
 Henry be tall , and broad , and fair , and weigh fifteen . but perhaps the 
 most curious - look of the three , take all the circumstance of the 
 case into consideration , be Captain John Good , R.N. there he sit upon 
 a leather bag , look just as though he have come in from a comfortable 
 day 's shooting in a civilised country , absolutely clean , tidy , and well 
 dress . he wear a shooting suit of brown tweed , with a hat to match , 
 and neat gaiter . as usual , he be beautifully shave , his eye - glass 
 and his false tooth appear to be in perfect order , and altogether he 
 look the neat man I ever have to do with in the wilderness . he even 
 sport a collar , of which he have a supply , make of white gutta - percha . 

 " you see , they weigh so little , " he say to I innocently , when I 
 express my astonishment at the fact ; " and I always like to turn out 
 like a gentleman . " ah ! if he could have foresee the future and the 
 raiment prepare for he . 

 well , there we three sit yarn away in the beautiful moonlight , and 
 watch the Kafirs a few yard off suck their intoxicate " daccha " 
 from a pipe of which the mouthpiece be make of the horn of an eland , 
 till one by one they roll themselves up in their blanket and go to 
 sleep by the fire , that is , all except Umbopa , who be a little apart , 
 his chin rest on his hand , and think deeply . I notice that he 
 never mix much with the other Kafirs . 

 presently , from the depth of the bush behind we , come a loud " woof , 
  woof ! " " that be a lion , " say I , and we all start up to listen . 
 hardly have we do so , when from the pool , about a hundred yard off , 
 we hear the strident trumpeting of an elephant . " Unkungunklovo ! 
  Indlovu ! " " Elephant ! elephant ! " whisper the Kafirs , and a few 
 minute afterwards we see a succession of vast shadowy form move 
 slowly from the direction of the water towards the bush . 

 up jump good , burn for slaughter , and thinking , perhaps , that it 
 be as easy to kill elephant as he have find it to shoot giraffe , but I 
 catch he by the arm and pull he down . 

 " it be no good , " I whisper , " let they go . " 

 " it seem that we be in a paradise of game . I vote we stop here a day 
 or two , and have a go at they , " say Sir Henry , presently . 

 I be rather surprised , for hitherto Sir Henry have always be for 
 push forward as fast as possible , more especially since we 
 ascertain at Inyati that about two year ago an Englishman of the 
 name of Neville have sell his wagon there , and go on up country . but 
 I suppose his hunter instinct get the well of he for a while . 

 Good jump at the idea , for he be long to have a shot at those 
 elephant ; and so , to speak the truth , do I , for it go against my 
 conscience to let such a herd as that escape without a pull at they . 

 " all right , my heartie , " say I. " I think we want a little recreation . 
 and now let us turn in , for we ought to be off by dawn , and then perhaps 
 we may catch they feed before they move on . " 

 the other agree , and we proceed to make our preparation . Good take 
 off his clothe , shake they , put his eye - glass and his false tooth into 
 his trouser pocket , and fold each article neatly , place it out of 
 the dew under a corner of his mackintosh sheet . Sir Henry and I 
 content ourselves with rougher arrangement , and soon be curl up 
 in our blanket , and drop off into the dreamless sleep that reward 
 the traveller . 

 go , go , go - what be that ? 

 suddenly , from the direction of the water come sound of violent 
 scuffling , and next instant there break upon our ear a succession of 
 the most awful roar . there be no mistake their origin ; only a lion 
 could make such a noise as that . we all jump up and look towards 
 the water , in the direction of which we see a confused mass , yellow and 
 black in colour , staggering and struggle towards we . we seize our 
 rifle , and slip on our veldtschoon , that be shoe make of 
 untanne hide , run out of the scherm . by this time the mass have fall , 
 and be roll over and over on the ground , and when we reach the 
 spot it struggle no long , but lie quite still . 

 now we see what it be . on the grass there lie a sable antelope 
 bull - the most beautiful of all the african antelope - quite dead , and 
 transfix by its great curved horn be a magnificent black - man 
 lion , also dead . evidently what have happen be this : the sable 
 antelope have come down to drink at the pool where the lion - no doubt 
 the same which we have hear - be lie in wait . while the antelope 
 drank , the lion have spring upon he , only to be receive upon the sharp 
 curve horn and transfix . once before I see a similar thing happen . 
 then the lion , unable to free himself , have tear and bite at the back 
 and neck of the bull , which , madden with fear and pain , have rush on 
 until it drop dead . 

 as soon as we have examine the beast sufficiently we call the 
 Kafirs , and between we manage to drag their carcase up to the scherm . 
 after that we go in and lie down , to wake no more till dawn . 

 with the first light we be up and make ready for the fray . we take 
 with we the three eight - bore rifle , a good supply of ammunition , and 
 our large water - bottle , fill with weak cold tea , which I have always 
 find the good stuff to shoot on . after swallow a little breakfast 
 we start , Umbopa , Khiva , and ventv"gel accompany we . the other 
 Kafirs we leave with instruction to skin the lion and the sable 
 antelope , and to cut up the latter . 

 we have no difficulty in find the broad elephant trail , which 
 Ventv"gel , after examination , pronounce to have be make by between 
 twenty and thirty elephant , most of they full - grow bull . but the 
 herd have move on some way during the night , and it be nine o'clock , 
 and already very hot , before , by the broken tree , bruised leaf and 
 bark , and smoke dropping , we know that we could not be far from they . 

 presently we catch sight of the herd , which number , as Ventv"gel have 
 say , between twenty and thirty , stand in a hollow , have finish 
 their morning meal , and flap their great ear . it be a splendid 
 sight , for they be only about two hundred yard from we . take a 
 handful of dry grass , I throw it into the air to see how the wind be ; 
 for if once they wind we I know they would be off before we could get 
 a shot . find that , if anything , it blow from the elephant to we , we 
 creep on stealthily , and thank to the cover manage to get within 
 forty yard or so of the great brute . just in front of we , and 
 broadside on , stand three splendid bull , one of they with enormous 
 tusk . I whisper to the other that I would take the middle one ; Sir 
 Henry cover the elephant to the left , and Good the bull with the big 
 tusk . 

 " now , " I whisper . 

 boom ! boom ! boom ! go the three heavy rifle , and down come Sir 
 Henry 's elephant dead as a hammer , shoot right through the heart . mine 
 fall on to its knee and I think that he be go to die , but in 
 another moment he be up and off , tear along straight past I . as he 
 go I give he the second barrel in the rib , and this bring he 
 down in good earnest . hastily slip in two fresh cartridge I run 
 close up to he , and a ball through the brain put an end to the poor 
 brute 's struggle . then I turn to see how good have fare with the big 
 bull , which I have hear scream with rage and pain as I give mine its 
 quietus . on reach the captain I find he in a great state of 
 excitement . it appear that on receive the bullet the bull have 
 turn and come straight for his assailant , who have barely time to get 
 out of his way , and then charge on blindly past he , in the direction 
 of our encampment . meanwhile the herd have crash off in wild alarm in 
 the other direction . 

 for awhile we debate whether to go after the wound bull or to follow 
 the herd , and finally decide for the latter alternative , depart , 
 think that we have see the last of those big tusk . I have often 
 wish since that we have . it be easy work to follow the elephant , for 
 they have leave a trail like a carriage road behind they , crush down 
 the thick bush in their furious flight as though it be tambouki grass . 

 but to come up with they be another matter , and we have struggle on 
 under the broiling sun for over two hour before we find they . with 
 the exception of one bull , they be stand together , and I could 
 see , from their unquiet way and the manner in which they keep lift 
 their trunk to test the air , that they be on the look - out for 
 mischief . the solitary bull stand fifty yard or so to this side of the 
 herd , over which he be evidently keep sentry , and about sixty yard 
 from we . think that he would see or wind we , and that it would 
 probably start they off again if we try to get near , especially as 
 the ground be rather open , we all aim at this bull , and at my 
 whisper word , we fire . the three shot take effect , and down he go 
 dead . again the herd start , but unfortunately for they about a 
 hundred yard far on be a nullah , or dry - out water track , with 
 steep bank , a place very much resemble the one where the Prince 
 Imperial be kill in Zululand . into this the elephant plunge , and 
 when we reach the edge we find they struggle in wild confusion to 
 get up the other bank , fill the air with their scream , and 
 trumpeting as they push one another aside in their selfish panic , 
 just like so many human being . now be our opportunity , and fire 
 away as quickly as we could load , we kill five of the poor beast , 
 and no doubt should have bag the whole herd , have they not suddenly 
 give up their attempt to climb the bank and rush headlong down the 
 nullah . we be too tired to follow they , and perhaps also a little 
 sick of slaughter , eight elephant be a pretty good bag for one day . 

 so after we be rest a little , and the Kafirs have cut out the heart 
 of two of the dead elephant for supper , we start homeward , very 
 well pleased with our day 's work , have make up our mind to send the 
 bearer on the morrow to chop away the tusk . 

 shortly after we re - pass the spot where Good have wound the 
 patriarchal bull we come across a herd of eland , but do not shoot at 
 they , as we have plenty of meat . they trot past we , and then stop 
 behind a little patch of bush about a hundred yard away , wheel 
 round to look at we . as Good be anxious to get a near view of they , 
 never have see an eland close , he hand his rifle to Umbopa , and , 
 follow by Khiva , stroll up to the patch of bush . we sit down and 
 wait for he , not sorry of the excuse for a little rest . 

 the sun be just go down in its reddest glory , and Sir Henry and I 
 be admire the lovely scene , when suddenly we hear an elephant 
 scream , and see its huge and rush form with uplifted trunk and tail 
 silhouette against the great fiery globe of the sun . next second we 
 see something else , and that be good and Khiva tear back towards we 
 with the wound bull - for it be he - charge after they . for a moment 
 we do not dare to fire - though at that distance it would have be of 
 little use if we have do so - for fear of hit one of they , and the 
 next a dreadful thing happen - Good fall a victim to his passion for 
 civilised dress . have he consent to discard his trouser and gaiter 
 like the rest of we , and to hunt in a flannel shirt and a pair of 
 veldt - schoon , it would have be all right . but as it be , his 
 trouser cumber he in that desperate race , and presently , when he 
 be about sixty yard from we , his boot , polish by the dry grass ,

 we give a gasp , for we know that he must die , and run as hard as we

 stick in his trunk . 

 with a scream of pain , the brute seize the poor Zulu , hurl he to 
 the earth , and place one huge foot on to his body about the middle , 
 twin its trunk round his upper part and tear he in two . 

 we rush up mad with horror , and fire again and again , till presently 
 the elephant fall upon the fragment of the Zulu . 

 as for Good , he rise and wrung his hand over the brave man who have 
 give his life to save he , and , though I be an old hand , I feel a lump 
 grow in my throat . Umbopa stand contemplate the huge dead elephant 
 and the mangle remain of poor Khiva . 

 " ah , well , " he say presently , " he be dead , but he die like a man ! " 



 CHAPTER V 

 OUR MARCH into the desert 

 we have kill nine elephant , and it take we two day to cut out the 
 tusk , and have bring they into camp , to bury they carefully in the 
 sand under a large tree , which make a conspicuous mark for mile round . 
 it be a wonderfully fine lot of ivory . I never see a well , average 
 as it do between forty and fifty pound a tusk . the tusk of the great 
 bull that kill poor Khiva scale one hundred and seventy pound the 
 pair , so nearly as we could judge . 

 as for Khiva himself , we bury what remain of he in an ant - bear 
 hole , together with an assegai to protect himself with on his journey 
 to a well world . on the third day we march again , hop that we 
 might live to return to dig up our bury ivory , and in due course , 
 after a long and wearisome tramp , and many adventure which I have not 
 space to detail , we reach Sitanda 's Kraal , near the Lukanga River , 
 the real starting - point of our expedition . very well do I recollect our 
 arrival at that place . to the right be a scatter native settlement 
 with a few stone cattle kraal and some cultivate land down by the 
 water , where these savage grow their scanty supply of grain , and 
 beyond it stretch great tract of wave " veld " cover with tall 
 grass , over which herd of the small game be wander . to the left 
 lie the vast desert . this spot appear to be the outpost of the fertile 
 country , and it would be difficult to say to what natural cause such 
 an abrupt change in the character of the soil be due . but so it be . 

 just below our encampment flow a little stream , on the farth side 
 of which be a stony slope , the same down which , twenty year before , I 
 have see poor Silvestre creep back after his attempt to reach 
 Solomon 's Mines , and beyond that slope begin the waterless desert , 
 cover with a species of karoo shrub . 

 it be evening when we pitch our camp , and the great ball of the sun 
 be sink into the desert , send glorious ray of many - colour 
 light fly all over its vast expanse . leave Good to superintend the 
 arrangement of our little camp , I take Sir Henry with I , and walk 
 to the top of the slope opposite , we gaze across the desert . the air 
 be very clear , and far , far away I could distinguish the faint blue 
 outline , here and there cap with white , of the Suliman Berg . 

 " there , " I say , " there be the wall round Solomon 's Mines , but God 
 know if we shall ever climb it . " 

 " my brother should be there , and if he be , I shall reach he somehow , " 
 say Sir Henry , in that tone of quiet confidence which mark the man . 

 " I hope so , " I answer , and turn to go back to the camp , when I see 
 that we be not alone . behind we , also gaze earnestly towards the 
 far - off mountain , stand the great Kafir Umbopa . 

 the Zulu speak when he see that I have observe he , address Sir 
 Henry , to whom he have attach himself . 

 " be it to that land that thou wouldst journey , Incubu ? "   a native word 
 meaning , I believe , an elephant , and the name give to Sir Henry by the 
 Kafirs , he say , point towards the mountain with his broad assegai . 

 I ask he sharply what he mean by address his master in that 
 familiar way . it be very well for native to have a name for one among 
 themselves , but it be not decent that they should call a white man by 
 their heathenish appellation to his face . the Zulu laugh a quiet 
 little laugh which anger I . 

 " how dost thou know that I be not the equal of the Inkosi whom I 
 serve ? " he say . " he be of a royal house , no doubt ; one can see it in 
 his size and by his mien ; so , mayhap , be I. at least , I be as great a 
 man . be my mouth , o Macumazahn , and say my word to the Inkoos Incubu , 
 my master , for I would speak to he and to thee . " 

 I be angry with the man , for I be not accustomed to be talk to in 
 that way by Kafirs , but somehow he impress I , and besides I be 
 curious to know what he have to say . so I translate , express my 
 opinion at the same time that he be an impudent fellow , and that his 
 swagger be outrageous . 

 " yes , Umbopa , " answer Sir Henry , " I would journey there . " 

 " the desert be wide and there be no water in it , the mountain be high 
 and cover with snow , and man can not say what lie beyond they behind 
 the place where the sun set ; how shalt thou come thither , Incubu , and 
 wherefore dost thou go ? " 

 I translate again . 

 " tell he , " answer Sir Henry , " that I go because I believe that a man 
 of my blood , my brother , have go there before I , and I journey to 
 seek he . " 

 " that be so , Incubu ; a Hottentot I meet on the road tell I that a white 
 man go out into the desert two year ago towards those mountain with 
 one servant , a hunter . they never come back . " 

 " how do you know it be my brother ? " ask Sir Henry . 

 " Nay , I know not . but the Hottentot , when I ask what the white man 
 be like , say that he have thine eye and a black beard . he say , too , 
 that the name of the hunter with he be Jim ; that he be a Bechuana 
 hunter and wear clothe . " 

 " there be no doubt about it , " say I ; " I know Jim well . " 

 Sir Henry nod . " I be sure of it , " he say . " if George set his mind 
 upon a thing he generally do it . it be always so from his boyhood . if 
 he mean to cross the Suliman Berg he have cross it , unless some 
 accident overtake he , and we must look for he on the other side . " 

 Umbopa understand English , though he rarely speak it . 

 " it be a far journey , Incubu , " he put in , and I translate his remark . 

 " yes , " answer Sir Henry , " it be far . but there be no journey upon 
 this earth that a man may not make if he set his heart to it . there be 
 nothing , Umbopa , that he can not do , there be no mountain he may not 
 climb , there be no desert he can not cross , save a mountain and a 
 desert of which you be spar the knowledge , if love lead he and he 
 hold his life in his hand count it as nothing , ready to keep it or 
 lose it as Heaven above may order . " 

 I translate . 

 " great word , my father , " answer the Zulu - I always call he a 
 Zulu , though he be not really one - " great swell word fit to fill 
 the mouth of a man . thou art right , my father Incubu . listen ! what be 
 life ? it be a feather , it be the seed of the grass , blow hither and 
 thither , sometimes multiply itself and die in the act , sometimes 
 carry away into the heaven . but if that seed be good and heavy it 
 may perchance travel a little way on the road it will . it be well to 
 try and journey one 's road and to fight with the air . man must die . at 
 the bad he can but die a little soon . I will go with thee across 
 the desert and over the mountain , unless perchance I fall to the 
 ground on the way , my father . " 

 he pause awhile , and then go on with one of those strange burst of 
 rhetorical eloquence that Zulus sometimes indulge in , which to my mind , 
 full though they be of vain repetition , show that the race be by no 
 mean devoid of poetic instinct and of intellectual power . 

 " what be life ? tell I , o white man , who be wise , who know the secret 
 of the world , and of the world of star , and the world that lie above 
 and around the star ; who flash your word from afar without a voice ; 
 tell I , white man , the secret of our life - whither it go and whence 
 it come ! 

 " you can not answer I ; you know not . listen , I will answer . out of the 
 dark we come , into the dark we go . like a storm - drive bird at night we 
 fly out of the Nowhere ; for a moment our wing be see in the light of 
 the fire , and , lo ! we be go again into the Nowhere . life be nothing . 
 life be all . it be the Hand with which we hold off death . it be the 
 glow - worm that shin in the night - time and be black in the morning ; it 
 be the white breath of the oxen in winter ; it be the little shadow that 
 run across the grass and lose itself at sunset . " 

 " you be a strange man , " say Sir Henry , when he have cease . 

 Umbopa laugh . " it seem to I that we be much alike , Incubu . perhaps 
  I seek a brother over the mountain . " 

 I look at he suspiciously . " what dost thou mean ? " I ask ; " what 
 dost thou know of those mountain ? " 

 " a little ; a very little . there be a strange land yonder , a land of 
 witchcraft and beautiful thing ; a land of brave people , and of tree , 
 and stream , and snowy peak , and of a great white road . I have hear 
 of it . but what be the good of talk ? it grow dark . those who live 
 to see will see . " 

 again I look at he doubtfully . the man know too much . 

 " you need not fear I , Macumazahn , " he say , interpret my look . " I 
 dig no hole for you to fall in . I make no plot . if ever we cross 
 those mountain behind the sun I will tell what I know . but Death sit 
 upon they . be wise and turn back . go and hunt elephant , my master . I 
 have speak . " 

 and without another word he lift his spear in salutation , and 
 return towards the camp , where shortly afterwards we find he 
 clean a gun like any other Kafir . 

 " that be an odd man , " say Sir Henry . 

 " yes , " answer I , " too odd by half . I do not   like his little way . he 
 know something , and will not speak out . but I suppose it be no use 
 quarrel with he . we be in for a curious trip , and a mysterious 
 Zulu will not   make much difference one way or another . " 

 next day we make our arrangement for start . of course it be 
 impossible to drag our heavy elephant rifle and other kit with we 
 across the desert , so , dismiss our bearer , we make an arrangement 
 with an old native who have a kraal close by to take care of they till 
 we return . it go to my heart to leave such thing as those sweet 
 tool to the tender mercy of an old thief of a savage whose greedy 
 eye I could see gloating over they . but I take some precaution . 

 first of all I load all the rifle , place they at full cock , and 
 inform he that if he touch they they would go off . he try the 
 experiment instantly with my eight - bore , and it do go off , and blow a 
 hole right through one of his oxen , which be just then be drive 
 up to the kraal , to say nothing of knock he head over heel with 
 the recoil . he get up considerably startle , and not at all pleased at 
 the loss of the ox , which he have the impudence to ask I to pay for , 
 and nothing would induce he to touch the gun again . 

 " put the live devil out of the way up there in the thatch , " he say , 
 " or they will murder we all . " 

 then I tell he that , when we come back , if one of those thing be 
 miss I would kill he and his people by witchcraft ; and if we die 
 and he try to steal the rifle I would come and haunt he and turn 
 his cattle mad and his milk sour till life be a weariness , and would 
 make the devil in the gun come out and talk to he in a way he do 
 not like , and generally give he a good idea of judgment to come . after 
 that he promise to look after they as though they be his father 's 
 spirit . he be a very superstitious old Kafir and a great villain . 

 have thus dispose of our superfluous gear we arrange the kit we 
 five - Sir Henry , Good , myself , Umbopa , and the Hottentot 
 ventv"gel - be to take with we on our journey . it be small enough , 
 but do what we would we could not get its weight down under about forty 
 pound a man . this be what it consist of : - 

 the three express rifle and two hundred round of ammunition . 

 the two Winchester repeating rifle   for Umbopa and Ventv"gel , with 
 two hundred round of cartridge . 

 five Cochrane 's water - bottle , each hold four pint . 

 five blanket . 

 twenty - five pound ' weight of biltong - i.e. sun - dry game flesh . 

 ten pound ' weight of good mixed bead for gift . 

 a selection of medicine , include an ounce of quinine , and one or two 
 small surgical instrument . 

 our knife , a few sundrie , such as a compass , match , a pocket 
 filter , tobacco , a trowel , a bottle of brandy , and the clothe we stand 
 in . 

 this be our total equipment , a small one indeed for such a venture , 
 but we dare not attempt to carry more . indeed , that load be a heavy 
 one per man with which to travel across the burn desert , for in such 
 place every additional ounce tell . but we could not see our way to 
 reduce the weight . there be nothing take but what be absolutely 
 necessary . 

 with great difficulty , and by the promise of a present of a good 
 hunting - knife each , I succeed in persuade three wretched native 
 from the village to come with we for the first stage , twenty mile , and 
 to carry a large gourd hold a gallon of water apiece . my object be 
 to enable we to refill our water - bottle after the first night 's march ,

 probable ; but be desirous of obtain the knife , which be almost 
 unknown treasure up there , they consent to come , have probably 
 reflect that , after all , our subsequent extinction would be no affair 
 of theirs . 

 all next day we rest and sleep , and at sunset eat a hearty meal of 
 fresh beef wash down with tea , the last , as Good remark sadly , we 
 be likely to drink for many a long day . then , have make our final 
 preparation , we lie down and wait for the moon to rise . at last , 
 about nine o'clock , up she come in all her glory , flood the wild 
 country with light , and throw a silver sheen on the expanse of 
 rolling desert before we , which look as solemn and quiet and as alien 
 to man as the star - stud firmament above . we rise up , and in a few 
 minute be ready , and yet we hesitate a little , as human nature be 
 prone to hesitate on the threshold of an irrevocable step . we three 
 white man stand by ourselves . Umbopa , assegai in hand and a rifle

 ahead of we ; while the hire native , with the gourd of water , and 
 Ventv"gel , be gather in a little knot behind . 

 " gentleman , " say Sir Henry presently , in his deep voice , " we be go 
 on about as strange a journey as man can make in this world . it be very 
 doubtful if we can succeed in it . but we be three man who will stand 
 together for good or for evil to the last . now before we start let we 
 for a moment pray to the Power who shape the destiny of man , and who 
 age since have mark out our path , that it may please he to direct 
 our step in accordance with his will . " 

 take off his hat , for the space of a minute or so , he cover his 
 face with his hand , and Good and I do likewise . 

 I do not say that I be a first - rate pray man , few hunter be , and 
 as for Sir Henry , I never hear he speak like that before , and only 
 once since , though deep down in his heart I believe that he be very 
 religious . good too be pious , though apt to swear . anyhow I do not 
 remember , except on one single occasion , ever put up a well 
 prayer in my life than I do during that minute , and somehow I feel the 
 happy for it . our future be so completely unknown , and I think that 
 the unknown and the awful always bring a man near to his maker . 

 " and now , " say Sir Henry , " trek ! " 

 so we start . 

 we have nothing to guide ourselves by except the distant mountain and 
 old José da Silvestre 's chart , which , consider that it be draw by 
 a die and half - distraught man on a fragment of linen three century 
 ago , be not a very satisfactory sort of thing to work with . still , 
 our sole hope of success depend upon it , such as it be . if we fail 
 in find that pool of bad water which the old Dom mark as be 
 situate in the middle of the desert , about sixty mile from our 
 starting - point , and as far from the mountain , in all probability we 
 must perish miserably of thirst . but to my mind the chance of our

 infinitesimal . even suppose that da Silvestra have mark the pool 
 correctly , what be there to prevent its have be dry up by the 
 sun generation ago , or trample in by game , or fill with the 
 drift sand ? 

 on we tramp silently as shade through the night and in the heavy 
 sand . the karoo bush catch our foot and retard we , and the sand 
 work into our veldtschoon and Good 's shooting - boot , so that every 
 few mile we have to stop and empty they ; but still the night keep 
 fairly cool , though the atmosphere be thick and heavy , give a sort 
 of creamy feel to the air , and we make fair progress . it be very 
 silent and lonely there in the desert , oppressively so indeed . good 
 feel this , and once begin to whistle " the Girl I leave behind I , " but 
 the note sound lugubrious in that vast place , and he give it up . 

 shortly afterwards a little incident occur which , though it startle 
 we at the time , give rise to a laugh . Good be lead , as the holder 
 of the compass , which , be a sailor , of course he understand 
 thoroughly , and we be toil along in single file behind he , when 
 suddenly we hear the sound of an exclamation , and he vanish . next 
 second there arise all around we a most extraordinary hubbub , snort , 
 groan , and wild sound of rush foot . in the faint light , too , we 
 could descry dim galloping form half hide by wreath of sand . the 
 native throw down their load and prepare to bolt , but remember 
 that there be nowhere to run to , they cast themselves upon the ground 
 and howl out that it be ghost . as for Sir Henry and myself , we 
 stand amazed ; nor be our amazement lessen when we perceive the form 
 of Good career off in the direction of the mountain , apparently 
 mount on the back of a horse and halloae wildly . in another second 
 he throw up his arm , and we hear he come to the earth with a thud . 

 then I see what have happen ; we have stumble upon a herd of sleep 
 quagga , on to the back of one of which Good actually have fall , and 
 the brute naturally enough get up and make off with he . call out to 
 the other that it be all right , I run towards good , much afraid lest 
 he should be hurt , but to my great relief I find he sit in the 
 sand , his eye - glass still fix firmly in his eye , rather shake and 
 very much frightened , but not in any way injure . 

 after this we travel on without any further misadventure till about 
 one o'clock , when we call a halt , and have drink a little water , 
 not much , for water be precious , and rest for half an hour , we 
 start again . 

 on , on we go , till at last the east begin to blush like the cheek of 
 a girl . then there come faint ray of primrose light , that change 
 presently to golden bar , through which the dawn glide out across the 
 desert . the star grow pale and pale still , till at last they 
 vanish ; the golden moon wax wan , and her mountain ridge stand out 
 against her sickly face like the bone on the cheek of a die man . 
 then come spear upon spear of light flash far away across the 
 boundless wilderness , pierce and fire the veil of mist , till the 
 desert be drape in a tremulous golden glow , and it be day . 

 still we do not halt , though by this time we should have be glad 
 enough to do so , for we know that when once the sun be fully up it 
 would be almost impossible for we to travel . at length , about an hour 
 later , we spy a little pile of boulder rise out of the plain , and 
 to this we drag ourselves . as luck would have it , here we find an 
 overhang slab of rock carpet beneath with smooth sand , which 
 afford a most grateful shelter from the heat . underneath this we 
 crept , and each of we have drunk some water and eat a bit of 
 biltong , we lie down and soon be sound asleep . 

 it be three o'clock in the afternoon before we wake , to find our 
 bearer prepare to return . they have see enough of the desert 
 already , and no number of knife would have tempt they to come a step 
 far . so we take a hearty drink , and have empty our 
 water - bottle , fill they up again from the gourd that they have 
 bring with they , and then watch they depart on their twenty mile ' 
 tramp home . 

 at half - past four we also start . it be lonely and desolate work , for 
 with the exception of a few ostrich there be not a single living 
 creature to be see on all the vast expanse of sandy plain . evidently 
 it be too dry for game , and with the exception of a deadly - look 
 cobra or two we see no reptile . one insect , however , we find 
 abundant , and that be the common or house fly . there they come , " not 
 as single spy , but in battalion , " as I think the Old Testament 1 
 say somewhere . he be an extraordinary insect be the house fly . go 
 where you will you find he , and so it must have be always . I have 
 see he enclose in amber , which be , I be tell , quite half a million 
 year old , look exactly like his descendant of to - day , and I have 
 little doubt but that when the last man lie die on the earth he will 
 be buzz round - if this event happen to occur in summer - watch 
 for an opportunity to settle on his nose . 

 at sunset we halt , wait for the moon to rise . at last she come up , 
 beautiful and serene as ever , and , with one halt about two o'clock in 
 the morning , we trudge on wearily through the night , till at last the 
 welcome sun put a period to our labour . we drink a little and flung 
 ourselves down on the sand , thoroughly tired out , and soon be all 
 asleep . there be no need to set a watch , for we have nothing to fear 
 from anybody or anything in that vast untenanted plain . our only 
 enemy be heat , thirst , and fly , but far rather would I have face 
 any danger from man or beast than that awful trinity . this time we be 
 not so lucky as to find a shelter rock to guard we from the glare of 
 the sun , with the result that about seven o'clock we wake up 
 experience the exact sensation one would attribute to a beefsteak on 
 a gridiron . we be literally be bake through and through . the 
 burn sun seem to be suck our very blood out of we . we sit up 
 and gasp . 

 " Phew , " say I , grab at the halo of fly which buzz cheerfully 
 round my head . the heat do not affect they . 

 " my word ! " say Sir Henry . 

 " it be hot ! " echo Good . 

 it be hot , indeed , and there be not a bit of shelter to be find . 
 look where we would there be no rock or tree , nothing but an unending 
 glare , render dazzle by the heated air that dance over the surface 
 of the desert as it dance over a red - hot stove . 

 " what be to be do ? " ask Sir Henry ; " we can not   stand this for long . " 

 we look at each other blankly . 

 " I have it , " say Good , " we must dig a hole , get in it , and cover 
 ourselves with the karoo bush . " 

 it do not seem a very promising suggestion , but at least it be well 
 than nothing , so we set to work , and , with the trowel we have bring 
 with we and the help of our hand , in about an hour we succeed in 
 delve out a patch of ground some ten foot long by twelve wide to the 
 depth of two foot . then we cut a quantity of low scrub with our 
 hunting - knife , and creep into the hole , pull it over we all , with 
 the exception of Ventv"gel , on whom , be a Hottentot , the heat have no 
 particular effect . this give we some slight shelter from the burning 
 ray of the sun , but the atmosphere in that amateur grave can be well 
 imagine than describe . the Black Hole of Calcutta must have be a 
 fool to it ; indeed , to this moment I do not know how we live through 
 the day . there we lay panting , and every now and again moisten our 
 lip from our scanty supply of water . have we follow our inclination 
 we should have finish all we possess in the first two hour , but we 
 be force to exercise the most rigid care , for if our water fail we 
 we know that very soon we must perish miserably . 

 but everything have an end , if only you live long enough to see it , and 
 somehow that miserable day wear on towards evening . about three o'clock 
 in the afternoon we determine that we could bear it no long . it 
 would be well to die walk that to be kill slowly by heat and 
 thirst in this dreadful hole . so take each of we a little drink from 
 our fast diminish supply of water , now warm to about the same 
 temperature as a man 's blood , we stagger forward . 

 we have then cover some fifty mile of wilderness . if the reader will 
 refer to the rough copy and translation of old da Silvestra 's map , he 
 will see that the desert be mark as measure forty league across , 
 and the " pan bad water " be set down as be about in the middle of it . 
 now forty league be one hundred and twenty mile , consequently we 
 ought at the most to be within twelve or fifteen mile of the water if 
 any should really exist . 

 through the afternoon we creep slowly and painfully along , scarcely 
 do more than a mile and a half in an hour . at sunset we rest 
 again , wait for the moon , and after drink a little manage to get 
 some sleep . 

 before we lie down , Umbopa point out to we a slight and indistinct 
 hillock on the flat surface of the plain about eight mile away . at the 
 distance it look like an ant - hill , and as I be drop off to sleep 
 I fall to wonder what it could be . 

 with the moon we march again , feel dreadfully exhaust , and 
 suffer torture from thirst and prickly heat . nobody who have not 
 feel it can know what we go through . we walk no long , we 
 stagger , now and again fall from exhaustion , and be oblige to 
 call a halt every hour or so . we have scarcely energy leave in we to 
 speak . up to this Good have chat and joke , for he be a merry fellow ; 
 but now he have not a joke in he . 

 at last , about two o'clock , utterly wear out in body and mind , we come 
 to the foot of the queer hill , or sand koppie , which at first sight 
 resemble a gigantic ant - heap about a hundred foot high , and cover 
 at the base nearly two acre of ground . 

 here we halt , and drive to it by our desperate thirst , suck down 
 our last drop of water . we have but half a pint a head , and each of we 
 could have drink a gallon . 

 then we lie down . just as I be drop off to sleep I hear Umbopa 
 remark to himself in Zulu - 

 " if we can not find water we shall all be dead before the moon rise 
 to - morrow . " 

 I shudder , hot as it be . the near prospect of such an awful death be 
 not pleasant , but even the thought of it could not keep I from 
 sleep .

 CHAPTER VI 

 WATER ! WATER ! 

 two hour later , that is , about four o'clock , I wake up , for so soon as 
 the first heavy demand of bodily fatigue have be satisfy , the 
 torture thirst from which I be suffer assert itself . I could 
 sleep no more . I have be dream that I be bath in a run 
 stream , with green bank and tree upon they , and I awake to find 
 myself in this arid wilderness , and to remember , as Umbopa have say , 
 that if we do not find water this day we must perish miserably . no 
 human creature could live long without water in that heat . I sit up and 
 rub my grimy face with my dry and horny hand , as my lip and 
 eyelid be stick together , and it be only after some friction and 
 with an effort that I be able to open they . it be not far from dawn , 
 but there be none of the bright feel of dawn in the air , which be 
 thick with a hot murkiness that I can not describe . the other be 
 still sleep . 

 presently it begin to grow light enough to read , so I draw out a little 
 pocket copy of the " Ingoldsby legend " which I have bring with I , and 
 read " the Jackdaw of Rheims . " when I get to where 

  " a nice little boy hold a golden ewer , 
  emboss , and fill with water as pure 
  as any that flow between Rheims and Namur , " 

 literally I smack my crack lip , or rather try to smack they . 
 the mere thought of that pure water make I mad . if the Cardinal have 
 be there with his bell , book , and candle , I would have whip in and 
 drunk his water up ; yes , even if he have fill it already with the sud 
 of soap " worthy of wash the hand of the Pope , " and I know that the 
 whole consecrated curse of the Catholic Church should fall upon I for 
 so do . I almost think that I must have be a little light - head 
 with thirst , weariness and the want of food ; for I fall to think how 
 astonish the Cardinal and his nice little boy and the jackdaw would 
 have look to see a burn up , brown - eye , grizzly - haired little 
 elephant hunter suddenly bind between they , put his dirty face into 
 the basin , and swallow every drop of the precious water . the idea 
 amuse I so much that I laugh or rather cackle aloud , which wake 
 the other , and they begin to rub their dirty face and drag their 
 gum - up lip and eyelid apart . 

 as soon as we be all well awake we begin to discuss the situation , 
 which be serious enough . not a drop of water be leave . we turn the 
 bottle upside down , and lick their top , but it be a failure ; they 
 be dry as a bone . good , who have charge of the flask of brandy , get it 
 out and look at it longingly ; but Sir Henry promptly take it away 
 from he , for to drink raw spirit would only have be to precipitate 
 the end . 

 " if we do not find water we shall die , " he say . 

 " if we can trust to the old Dom 's map there should be some about , " I 
 say ; but nobody seem to derive much satisfaction from this remark . 
 it be so evident that no great faith could be put in the map . now it 
 be gradually grow light , and as we sit star blankly at each 
 other , I observe the Hottentot ventv"gel rise and begin to walk about 
 with his eye on the ground . presently he stop short , and utter a 
 guttural exclamation , point to the earth . 

 " what be it ? " we exclaim ; and rise simultaneously we go to where 
 he be stand star at the sand . 

 " well , " I say , " it be fresh Springbok spoor ; what of it ? " 

 " springbuck do not go far from water , " he answer in Dutch . 

 " no , " I answer , " I forget ; and thank God for it . " 

 this little discovery put new life into we ; for it be wonderful , when a 
 man be in a desperate position , how he catch at the slight hope , 
 and feel almost happy . on a dark night a single star be well than 
 nothing . 

 meanwhile ventv"gel be lift his snub nose , and sniff the hot air 
 for all the world like an old Impala ram who scent danger . presently 
 he speak again . 

 " I smell water , " he say . 

 then we feel quite jubilant , for we know what a wonderful instinct 
 these wild - breed man possess . 

 just at that moment the sun come up gloriously , and reveal so grand a 
 sight to our astonished eye that for a moment or two we even forget 
 our thirst . 

 there , not more than forty or fifty mile from we , glitter like 
 silver in the early ray of the morning sun , soar Sheba 's Breasts ; 
 and stretch away for hundred of mile on either side of they run 
 the great Suliman Berg . now that , sit here , I attempt to describe 
 the extraordinary grandeur and beauty of that sight , language seem to 
 fail I . I be impotent even before its memory . straight before we , rise 
 two enormous mountain , the like of which be not , I believe , to be 
 see in Africa , if indeed there be any other such in the world , 
 measure each of they at least fifteen thousand foot in height , 
 stand not more than a dozen mile apart , link together by a 
 precipitous cliff of rock , and tower in awful white solemnity 
 straight into the sky . these mountain place thus , like the pillar of 
 a gigantic gateway , be shape after the fashion of a woman 's breast , 
 and at time the mist and shadow beneath they take the form of a 
 recumbent woman , veil mysteriously in sleep . their basis swell gently 
 from the plain , look at that distance perfectly round and smooth ; 
 and upon the top of each be a vast hillock cover with snow , exactly 
 correspond to the nipple on the female breast . the stretch of cliff 
 that connect they appear to be some thousand of foot in height , and 
 perfectly precipitous , and on each flank of they , so far as the eye can 
 reach , extent similar line of cliff , break only here and there by 
 flat table - top mountain , something like the world - fame one at Cape 
 Town ; a formation , by the way , that be very common in Africa . 

 to describe the comprehensive grandeur of that view be beyond my 
 power . there be something so inexpressibly solemn and overpower 
 about those huge volcano - for doubtless they be extinct 
 volcano - that it quite awe we . for a while the morning light play 
 upon the snow and the brown and swell mass beneath , and then , as 
 though to veil the majestic sight from our curious eye , strange 
 vapour and cloud gather and increase around the mountain , till 
 presently we could only trace their pure and gigantic outline , show 
 ghostlike through the fleecy envelope . indeed , as we afterwards 
 discover , usually they be wrap in this gauze - like mist , which 
 doubtless account for our not have see they more clearly before . 

 Sheba 's Breasts have scarcely vanish into cloud - clothe privacy , before 
 our thirst - literally a burn question - reassert itself . 

 it be all very well for ventv"gel to say that he smell water , but we 
 could see no sign of it , look which way we would . so far as the eye 
 might reach there be nothing but arid swelter sand and karoo scrub . 
 we walk round the hillock and gaze about anxiously on the other 
 side , but it be the same story , not a drop of water could be find ; 
 there be no indication of a pan , a pool , or a spring . 

 " you be a fool , " I say angrily to Ventv"gel ; " there be no water . " 

 but still he lift his ugly snub nose and sniff . 

 " I smell it , Baas , " he answer ; " it be somewhere in the air . " 

 " yes , " I say , " no doubt it be in the cloud , and about two month 
 hence it will fall and wash our bone . " 

 Sir Henry stroke his yellow beard thoughtfully . " perhaps it be on the 
 top of the hill , " he suggest . 

 " rot , " say good ; " whoever hear of water be find at the top of a 
 hill ! " 

 " let we go and look , " I put in , and hopelessly enough we scramble up 
 the sandy side of the hillock , Umbopa leading . presently he stop as 
 though he be petrify . 

 " Nanzia manzie ! " that be , " here be water ! " he cry with a loud voice . 

 we rush up to he , and there , sure enough , in a deep cut or 
 indentation on the very top of the sand koppie , be an undoubted pool 
 of water . how it come to be in such a strange place we do not stop to 
 inquire , nor do we hesitate at its black and unpleasant appearance . it 
 be water , or a good imitation of it , and that be enough for we . we 
 give a bound and a rush , and in another second we be all down on our 
 stomach suck up the uninviting fluid as though it be nectar fit 
 for the god . heaven , how we do drink ! then when we have do drinking 
 we tear off our clothe and sit down in the pool , absorb the 
 moisture through our parch skin . you , Harry , my boy , who have only 
 to turn on a couple of tap to summon " hot " and " cold " from an unseen , 
 vasty cistern , can have little idea of the luxury of that muddy wallow 
 in brackish tepid water . 

 after a while we rise from it , refresh indeed , and fall to on our 
 " biltong , " of which we have scarcely be able to touch a mouthful for

 CHAPTER VII 

 SOLOMON 'S ROAD 

 outside the cavern we halt , feel rather foolish .

 take the piece of fat with which he have grease his boot , good 
 wash it thoroughly in the stream . then diving again into the bag he

 Good spring up with a profane exclamation   if it have not be a safety

 " greeting , " answer the old man , not , indeed , in the same tongue , but

 " what do that beggar say ? " ask Good .

 " oh , Lord ! " groan Good ; and , as be his way when perplex , he put

 " what be up ? " say I. 

 " it be his tooth , " whisper Sir Henry excitedly . " he move they . take 
 they out , good , take they out ! " 

 he obey , slip the set into the sleeve of his flannel shirt . 

 in another second curiosity have overcome fear , and the man advance

 kill we . 

 " how be it , O stranger , " ask the old man solemnly , " that this fat 
 man   pointing to Good , who be clothe in nothing but boot and a flannel

 now the young man who have fling the knife throw himself down on the

 " I see that ye be spirit , " he say falteringly ; " do ever man bear of

 here be luck indeed , and , needless to say , I jump at the chance . 

 " it be grant , " I say with an imperial smile . " Nay , ye shall know the

 " oh ! oh ! " groan the chorus of astonished aborigine . 

 " yes , " I go on , " we do , indeed " ; and again I smile benignly , as I 
 utter that amazing lie . " we come to stay with you a little while , and

 prepare myself for this visit by the learning of your language . "

 " only , my lord , " put in the old gentleman , " thou hast learn it very 
 badly . " 

 I cast an indignant glance at he , and he quail . 

 " now friend , " I continue , " ye might think that after so long a 
 journey we should find it in our heart to avenge such a reception , 
 mayhap to strike cold in death the imperious hand that - that , in

 king 's son , and I be his uncle . if anything befall he his blood will 
 be require at my hand . " 

 " yes , that be certainly so , " put in the young man with great emphasis . 

 " Ye may perhaps doubt our power to avenge , " I go on , heedless of this 
 by - play . " stay , I will show you . here , thou dog and slave   address 
 Umbopa in a savage tone , give I the magic tube that speak " ; and I 
 tip a wink towards my express rifle . 

 Umbopa rise to the occasion , and with something as nearly resemble a 
 grin as I have ever see on his dignified face he hand I the gun . 

 " it be here , o Lord of Lords , " he say with a deep obeisance . 

 now just before I have ask for the rifle I have perceive a little 
  klipspringer antelope stand on a mass of rock about seventy yard 
 away , and determine to risk the shot . 

 " ye see that buck , " I say , point the animal out to the party before 
 I . " tell I , be it possible for man bear of woman to kill it from here 
 with a noise ? " 

 " it be not possible , my lord , " answer the old man . 

 " yet shall I kill it , " I say quietly . 

 the old man smile . " that my lord can not do , " he answer . 

 I raise the rifle and cover the buck . it be a small animal , and one 
 which a man might well be excuse for miss , but I know that it would 
 not do to miss . 

 I draw a deep breath , and slowly press on the trigger . the buck stand 
 still as a stone . 

 " Bang ! thud ! " the antelope spring into the air and fall on the rock 
 dead as a door nail . 

 a groan of simultaneous terror burst from the group before we . 

 " if you want meat , " I remark coolly , " go fetch that buck . " 

 the old man make a sign , and one of his follower depart , and 
 presently return bear the klipspringer . I notice with 
 satisfaction that I have hit it fairly behind the shoulder . they

 " ye see , " I say , " I do not speak empty word . " 

 there be no answer . 

 " if ye yet doubt our power , " I go on , " let one of you go stand upon 
 that rock that I may make he as this buck . " 

 none of they seem at all inclined to take the hint , till at last the 
 king 's son speak . 

 " it be well say . do thou , my uncle , go stand upon the rock . it be but 
 a buck that the magic have kill . surely it can not kill a man . " 

 the old gentleman do not take the suggestion in good part . indeed , he 
 seem hurt . 

 " no ! no ! " he ejaculate hastily , " my old eye have see enough . these 
 be wizard , indeed . let we bring they to the king . yet if any should 
 wish a further proof , let he stand upon the rock , that the magic 
 tube may speak with he . " 

 there be a most general and hasty expression of dissent . 

 " let not good magic be waste on our poor body , " say one ; " we be 
 satisfied . all the witchcraft of our people can not show the like of 
 this . " 

 " it be so , " remark the old gentleman , in a tone of intense relief ; 
 " without any doubt it be so . listen , child of the Stars , child of 
 the shin Eye and the movable Teeth , who roar out in thunder , and 
 slay from afar . I be Infadoos , son of Kafa , once king of the Kukuana 
 people . this youth be Scragga . " 

 " he nearly scrag I , " murmur Good . 

 " Scragga , son of Twala , the great king - Twala , husband of a thousand 
 wife , chief and lord paramount of the Kukuanas , keeper of the great 
 Road , terror of his enemy , student of the Black Arts , leader of a 
 hundred thousand warrior , Twala the one - eye , the Black , the terrible . " 

 " so , " say I superciliously , " lead we then to Twala . we do not talk 
 with low people and underling . " 

 " it be well , my lord , we will lead you ; but the way be long . we be 
 hunt three day ' journey from the place of the king . but let my 
 lord have patience , and we will lead they . " 

 " so be it , " I say carelessly ; " all time be before we , for we do not 
 die . we be ready , lead on . but Infadoos , and thou Scragga , beware ! 
 play we no monkey trick , set for we no fox ' snare , for before your

 face shall destroy you , and go through your land ; his vanish tooth

 and child ; the magic tube shall argue with you loudly , and make you 
 as sieve . beware ! " 

 this magnificent address do not fail of its effect ; indeed , it might 
 almost have be spar , so deeply be our friend already impress

 the old man make a deep obeisance , and murmur the word , " Koom 
 Koom , " which I afterwards discover be their royal salute , 
 correspond to the Bayéte of the Zulus , and turning , address his

 chattel , in order to bear they for we , except only the gun , which

 " let not my lord of the transparent Eye and the melt Teeth touch

 " but I want to put them on ! " roar Good , in nervous English . 

 Umbopa translate . 

 " Nay , my lord , " answer Infadoos , " would my lord cover up his 
 beautiful white leg   although he be so dark good have a singularly 
 white skin   from the eye of his servant ? have we offend my lord 
 that he should do such a thing ? " 

 here I nearly explode with laughing ; and meanwhile one of the man 
 start on with the garment . 

 " damn it ! " roar Good , " that black villain have get my trouser . " 

 " look here , good , " say Sir Henry ; " you have appear in this country 
 in a certain character , and you must live up to it . it will never do 
 for you to put on trouser again . henceforth you must exist in a 
 flannel shirt , a pair of boot , and an eye - glass . " 

 " yes , " I say , " and with whisker on one side of your face and not on 
 the other . if you change any of these thing the people will think that 
 we be impostor . I be very sorry for you , but , seriously , you must . if 
 once they begin to suspect we our life will not be worth a brass

 " do you really think so ? " say Good gloomily . 

 " I do , indeed . your ' beautiful white leg ' and your eye - glass be now 
  the feature of our party , and as Sir Henry say , you must live up to 
 they . be thankful that you have get your boot on , and that the air be 
 warm . " 

 Good sigh , and say no more , but it take he a fortnight to become 
 accustomed to his new and scant attire . 



 CHAPTER VIII 

 we enter KUKUANALAND 

 all that afternoon we travel along the magnificent roadway , which 
 trend steadily in a north - westerly direction . Infadoos and Scragga 
 walk with we , but their follower march about one hundred pace 
 ahead . 

 " Infadoos , " I say at length , " who make this road ? " 

 " it be make , my lord , of old time , none know how or when , not even the 
 wise woman Gagool , who have live for generation . we be not old enough 
 to remember its making . none can fashion such road now , but the king 
 suffer no grass to grow upon it . " 

 " and whose be the writing on the wall of the cave through which we 
 have pass on the road ? " I ask , refer to the Egyptian - like 
 sculpture that we have see . 

 " my lord , the hand that make the road write the wonderful writing . we 
 know not who write they . " 

 " when do the Kukuana people come into this country ? " 

 " my lord , the race come down here like the breath of a storm ten 
 thousand thousand moon ago , from the great land which lie there 
 beyond , " and he point to the north . " they could travel no far 
 because of the high mountain which ring in the land , so say the old 
 voice of our father that have descend to we the child , and so 
 say Gagool , the wise woman , the smeller out of witch , " and again he 
 point to the snow - clothe peak . " the country , too , be good , so they 
 settle here and grow strong and powerful , and now our number be like 
 the sea sand , and when Twala the king call up his regiment their 
 plume cover the plain so far as the eye of man can reach . " 

 " and if the land be wall in with mountain , who be there for the 
 regiment to fight with ? " 

 " Nay , my lord , the country be open there towards the north , and now and 
 again warrior sweep down upon we in cloud from a land we know not , 
 and we slay they . it be the third part of the life of a man since there 
 be a war . many thousand die in it , but we destroy those who come 
 to eat we up . so since then there have be no war . " 

 " your warrior must grow weary of rest on their spear , Infadoos . " 

 " my lord , there be one war , just after we destroy the people that 
 come down upon we , but it be a civil war ; dog eat dog . " 

 " how be that ? " 

 " my lord the king , my half - brother , have a brother bear at the same 
 birth , and of the same woman . it be not our custom , my lord , to suffer 
 twin to live ; the weak must always die . but the mother of the king 
 hide away the feebler child , which be bear the last , for her heart 
 yearn over it , and that child be Twala the king . I be his young 
 brother , bear of another wife . " 

 " well ? " 

 " my lord , Kafa , our father , die when we come to manhood , and my 
 brother Imotu be make king in his place , and for a space reign and 
 have a son by his favourite wife . when the babe be three year old , 
 just after the great war , during which no man could sow or reap , a 
 famine come upon the land , and the people murmur because of the 
 famine , and look round like a starve lion for something to rend . 
 then it be that Gagool , the wise and terrible woman , who do not die , 
 make a proclamation to the people , say , ' the king Imotu be no king . ' 
 and at the time Imotu be sick with a wound , and lie in his kraal not 
 able to move . 

 " then Gagool go into a hut and lead out Twala , my half - brother , and 
 twin brother to the king , whom she have hide among the cave and rock 
 since he be bear , and strip the ' moocha '   waist - cloth   off his 
 loin , show the people of the Kukuanas the mark of the sacred snake 
 coil round his middle , wherewith the eld son of the king be mark 
 at birth , and cry out loud , ' behold your king whom I have save for 
 you even to this day ! ' 

 " now the people be mad with hunger , and altogether bereft of reason 
 and the knowledge of truth , cry out - ' the king ! the king ! ' but I 
 know that it be not so , for Imotu my brother be the elder of the 
 twin , and our lawful king . then just as the tumult be at its height 
 Imotu the king , though he be very sick , crawl from his hut hold 
 his wife by the hand , and follow by his little son Ignosi - that be , 
 by interpretation , the Lightning . 

 " ' what be this noise ? ' he ask . ' why cry ye the king ! the king ! ' 

 " then Twala , his twin brother , bear of the same woman , and in the same 
 hour , run to he , and take he by the hair , stab he through the 
 heart with his knife . and the people be fickle , and ever ready to 
 worship the rise sun , clap their hand and cry , ' Twala be 
 king ! now we know that Twala be king ! ' " 

 " and what become of Imotu 's wife and her son Ignosi ? do Twala kill 
 they too ? " 

 " Nay , my lord . when she see that her lord be dead the queen seize the 
 child with a cry and run away . two day afterward she come to a kraal 
 very hungry , and none would give her milk or food , now that her lord 
 the king be dead , for all man hate the unfortunate . but at nightfall a 
 little child , a girl , creep out and bring her corn to eat , and she 
 bless the child , and go on towards the mountain with her boy 
 before the sun rise again , and there she must have perish , for none 
 have see she since , nor the child Ignosi . " 

 " then if this child Ignosi have live he would be the true king of the 
 Kukuana people ? " 

 " that be so , my lord ; the sacred snake be round his middle . if he live 
 he be king ; but , alas ! he be long dead . " 

 " see , my lord , " and Infadoos point to a vast collection of hut 
 surround by a fence , which be in its turn encircle by a great 
 ditch , that lie on the plain beneath we . " that be the kraal where the 
 wife of Imotu be last see with the child Ignosi . it be there that we 
 shall sleep to - night , if , indeed , " he add doubtfully , " my lord sleep 
 at all upon this earth . " 

 " when we be among the Kukuanas , my good friend Infadoos , we do as the 
 Kukuanas do , " I say majestically , and turn round quickly to address 
 Good , who be tramp along sullenly behind , his mind fully occupy 
 with unsatisfactory attempt to prevent his flannel shirt from flap 
 in the evening breeze . to my astonishment I butt into Umbopa , who be 
 walk along immediately behind I , and very evidently have be 
 listen with the great interest to my conversation with Infadoos . 
 the expression on his face be most curious , and give I the idea of a 
 man who be struggle with partial success to bring something long ago 
 forget back into his mind . 

 all this while we have be press on at a good rate towards the 
 undulating plain beneath we . the mountain we have cross now loom 
 high above our head , and Sheba 's Breasts be veil modestly in 
 diaphanous wreath of mist . as we go the country grow more and more 
 lovely . the vegetation be luxuriant , without be tropical ; the sun 
 be bright and warm , but not burn ; and a gracious breeze blow softly 
 along the odorous slope of the mountain . indeed , this new land be 
 little less than an earthly paradise ; in beauty , in natural wealth , and 
 in climate I have never see its like . the Transvaal be a fine country , 
 but it be nothing to Kukuanaland . 

 so soon as we start Infadoos have despatch a runner to warn the 
 people of the kraal , which , by the way , be in his military command , of 
 our arrival . this man have depart at an extraordinary speed , which 
 Infadoos inform I he would keep up all the way , as run be an 
 exercise much practise among his people . 

 the result of this message now become apparent . when we arrive within 
 two mile of the kraal we could see that company after company of man 
 be issue from its gate and march towards we . 

 Sir Henry lay his hand upon my arm , and remark that it look as 
 though we be go to meet with a warm reception . something in his 
 tone attract Infadoos ' attention . 

 " let not my lord be afraid , " he say hastily , " for in my breast there 
 dwell no guile . this regiment be one under my command , and come out 
 by my order to greet you . " 

 I nod easily , though I be not quite easy in my mind . 

 about half a mile from the gate of this kraal be a long stretch of 
 rise ground slop gently upwards from the road , and here the 
 company form . it be a splendid sight to see they , each company 
 about three hundred strong , charge swiftly up the rise , with flash 
 spear and wave plume , to take their appoint place . by the time we 
 reach the slope twelve such company , or in all three thousand six 
 hundred man , have pass out and take up their position along the road . 

 presently we come to the first company , and be able to gaze in 
 astonishment on the most magnificent set of warrior that I have ever 
 see . they be all man of mature age , mostly veteran of about forty , 
 and not one of they be under six foot in height , whilst many stand six 
 foot three or four . they wear upon their head heavy black plume of 
 Sakaboola feather , like those which adorn our guide . about their 
 waist and beneath the right knee be bind circlet of white ox 
 tail , while in their left hand they carry round shield measure 
 about twenty inch across . these shield be very curious . the 
 framework be make of an iron plate beat out thin , over which be 
 stretch milk - white ox - hide . 

 the weapon that each man bore be simple , but most effective , 
 consist of a short and very heavy two - edge spear with a wooden 
 shaft , the blade be about six inch across at the wide part . 
 these spear be not use for throw but like the Zulu " bangwan , " 
 or stab assegai , be for close quarter only , when the wound 
 inflict by they be terrible . in addition to his bangwan every man 
 carry three large and heavy knife , each knife weigh about two 
 pound . one knife be fix in the ox - tail girdle , and the other two at 
 the back of the round shield . these knife , which be call " tollas " 
 by the Kukuanas , take the place of the throw assegai of the Zulus . 
 the Kukuana warrior can cast they with great accuracy to a distance of 
 fifty yard , and it be their custom on charge to hurl a volley of 
 they at the enemy as they come to close quarter . 

 each company remain still as a collection of bronze statue till we 
 be opposite to it , when at a signal give by its commanding officer , 
 who , distinguish by a leopard skin cloak , stand some pace in front , 
 every spear be raise into the air , and from three hundred throat 
 spring forth with a sudden roar the royal salute of " Koom . " then , so 
 soon as we have pass , the company form up behind we and follow we 
 towards the kraal , till at last the whole regiment of the " Greys " - so 
 call from their white shield - the crack corps of the Kukuana people , 
 be march in our rear with a tread that shake the ground . 

 at length , branch off from Solomon 's Great Road , we come to the wide 
 fosse surround the kraal , which be at least a mile round , and fence 
 with a strong palisade of pile form of the trunk of tree . at the 
 gateway this fosse be span by a primitive drawbridge , which be let 
 down by the guard to allow we to pass in . the kraal be exceedingly well 
 lay out . through the centre run a wide pathway intersect at right 
 angle by other pathway so arrange as to cut the hut into square 
 block , each block be the quarter of a company . the hut be 
 dome - shape , and build , like those of the Zulus , of a framework of 
 wattle , beautifully thatch with grass ; but , unlike the Zulu hut , 
 they have doorway through which man could walk . also they be much 
 large , and surround by a verandah about six foot wide , beautifully 
 pave with powdered lime trodden hard . 

 all along each side of this wide pathway that pierce the kraal be 
 range hundred of woman , bring out by curiosity to look at we . these 
 woman , for a native race , be exceedingly handsome . they be tall and 
 graceful , and their figure be wonderfully fine . the hair , though 
 short , be rather curly than woolly , the feature be frequently 
 aquiline , and the lip be not unpleasantly thick , as be the case among 
 most african race . but what strike we most be their exceedingly quiet 
 and dignified air . they be as well - breed in their way as the 
  habituées of a fashionable drawing - room , and in this respect they 
 differ from Zulu woman and their cousin the Masai who inhabit the 
 district beyond Zanzibar . their curiosity have bring they out to see 
 we , but they allow no rude expression of astonishment or savage 
 criticism to pass their lip as we trudge wearily in front of they . 
 not even when old Infadoos with a surreptitious motion of the hand 
 point out the crown wonder of poor Good 's " beautiful white leg , " 
 do they suffer the feeling of intense admiration which evidently 
 master their mind to find expression . they fix their dark eye 
 upon this new and snowy loveliness , for , as I think I have say , Good 's 
 skin be exceedingly white , and that be all . but it be quite enough 
 for Good , who be modest by nature . 

 when we reach the centre of the kraal , Infadoos halt at the door of 
 a large hut , which be surround at a distance by a circle of small 
 one . 

 " Enter , Sons of the star , " he say , in a magniloquent voice , " and 
 deign to rest awhile in our humble habitation . a little food shall be 
 bring to you , so that ye may have no need to draw your belt tight 
 from hunger ; some honey and some milk , and an ox or two , and a few 
 sheep ; not much , my lord , but still a little food . " 

 " it be good , " say I. " Infadoos ; we be weary with travel through 
 realm of air ; now let we rest . " 

 accordingly we enter the hut , which we find amply prepare for our 
 comfort . couch of tanned skin be spread for we to lie on , and 
 water be place for we to wash in . 

 presently we hear a shouting outside , and step to the door , see a 
 line of damsel bear milk and roasted mealie , and honey in a pot . 
 behind these be some youth drive a fat young ox . we receive the 
 gift , and then one of the young man draw the knife from his girdle and 
 dexterously cut the ox 's throat . in ten minute it be dead , skin , 
 and joint . the good of the meat be then cut off for we , and the 
 rest , in the name of our party , I present to the warrior round we , 
 who take it and distribute the " white lord ' gift . " 

 Umbopa set to work , with the assistance of an extremely prepossess 
 young woman , to boil our portion in a large earthenware pot over a fire 
 which be build outside the hut , and when it be nearly ready we send a 
 message to Infadoos , and ask he and Scragga , the king 's son , to join 
 we . 

 presently they come , and sit down upon little stool , of which 
 there be several about the hut , for the Kukuanas do not in general 
 squat upon their haunch like the Zulus , they help we to get through 
 our dinner . the old gentleman be most affable and polite , but it 
 strike I that the young one regard we with doubt . together with the 
 rest of the party , he have be overawe by our white appearance and by 
 our magic property ; but it seem to I that , on discover that we 
 ate , drank , and sleep like other mortal , his awe be begin to wear 
 off , and to be replace by a sullen suspicion - which make I feel 
 rather uncomfortable . 

 in the course of our meal Sir Henry suggest to I that it might be 
 well to try to discover if our host know anything of his brother 's 
 fate , or if they have ever see or hear of he ; but , on the whole , I 
 think that it would be wise to say nothing of the matter at this 
 time . it be difficult to explain a relative lose from " the Stars . " 

 after supper we produce our pipe and light they ; a proceeding which 
 fill Infadoos and Scragga with astonishment . the Kukuanas be 
 evidently unacquainted with the divine delight of tobacco - smoke . the 
 herb be grow among they extensively ; but , like the Zulus , they use it 
 for snuff only , and quite fail to identify it in its new form . 

 presently I ask Infadoos when we be to proceed on our journey , and 
 be delighted to learn that preparation have be make for we to leave 
 on the follow morning , messenger have already depart to inform 
 Twala the king of our come . 

 it appear that Twala be at his principal place , know as Loo , make 
 ready for the great annual feast which be to be hold in the first week 
 of June . at this gathering all the regiment , with the exception of 
 certain detachment leave behind for garrison purpose , be bring up 
 and parade before the king ; and the great annual witch - hunt , of which 
 more by - and - by , be hold . 

 we be to start at dawn ; and Infadoos , who be to accompany we , 
 expect that we should reach Loo on the night of the second day ,

 CHAPTER ix 

 twala the king 

 it will not be necessary for I to detail at length the incident of 
 our journey to Loo . it take two full day ' travel along Solomon 's

 guard by ample garrison of troop . indeed , in Kukuanaland , as among 
 the Germans , the Zulus , and the Masai , every able - bodied man be a 
 soldier , so that the whole force of the nation be available for its 
 war , offensive or defensive . as we travel we be overtake by 
 thousand of warrior hurry up to Loo to be present at the great 
 annual review and festival , and more splendid troop I never see .

 slowly the sun sink , then suddenly darkness rush down on the land
