 CHAPTER X 

 the WITCH - HUNT 

 on reach our hut I motion to Infadoos to enter with we .

 we give a sign

 " very good ; then here we have it - ' 4 June , total eclipse of the moon

  c. ' there be a sign for you . tell they we will darken the moon

 the idea be a splendid one ; indeed , the only weak spot about it be a

 " I see no reason to suppose anything of the sort , " be his answer .

 know our exact position ; and I make out that the eclipse should

 " great man of the Kukuanas , and thou , Infadoos , listen . we love not to

 " ay , " say the old chief , still smile a little , " the people will

 " two mile from Loo , " go on Infadoos , " there be a hill curve like a

 " it be good , " say I. " let leave we to sleep awhile and to make ready

 infadoo rise , and , have salute we , depart with the chief . 

 " my friend , " say Ignosi , so soon as they be go , " can ye do this

 the big man with a smile . " what be it ? " 

 " this : that if ever you come to be king of this people you will do away 
 with the smelling out of wizard such as we see last night ; and that 
 the killing of man without trial shall no long take place in the 
 land . " 

 Ignosi think for a moment after I have translate this request , and 
 then answer - 

 " the way of black people be not as the way of white man , Incubu , nor 
 do we value life so highly . yet I will promise . if it be in my power to 
 hold they back , the witch - finder shall hunt no more , nor shall any man 
 die the death without trial or judgment . " 

 " that be a bargain , then , " say Sir Henry ; " and now let we get a little 
 rest . " 

 thoroughly weary out , we be soon sound asleep , and sleep till 
 Ignosi wake we about eleven o'clock . then we rise , wash , and eat a 
 hearty breakfast . after that we go outside the hut and walk about , 
 amuse ourselves with examine the structure of the Kukuana hut and 
 observe the custom of the woman . 

 " I hope that eclipse will come off , " say Sir Henry presently . 

 " if it do not it will soon be all up with we , " I answer mournfully ; 
 " for so sure as we be live man some of those chief will tell the 
 whole story to the king , and then there will be another sort of 
 eclipse , and one that we shall certainly not like . " 

 return to the hut we eat some dinner , and pass the rest of the day 
 in receive visit of ceremony and curiosity . at length the sun set , 
 and we enjoy a couple of hour of such quiet as our melancholy 
 foreboding would allow to we . finally , about half - past eight , a 
 messenger come from Twala to bid we to the great annual " dance of 
 girl " which be about to be celebrate . 

 hastily we put on the chain shirt that the king have send we , and

 before . 

 Twala greet we with much apparent cordiality , though I see he fix 
 his one eye viciously on Umbopa . 

 " welcome , white man from the star , " he say ; " this be another sight 
 from that which your eye gaze on by the light of last night 's moon ,

 this day ; but man be well . kiss and the tender word of woman be

 have they , as many as ye will , " and he pause for an answer . 

 as the prospect do not seem to be without attraction for Good , who , 
 like most sailor , be of a susceptible nature , - be elderly and wise , 
 foresee the endless complication that anything of the sort would 
 involve , for woman bring trouble so surely as the night follow the 
 day , I put in a hasty answer - 

 " thank to thee , o king , but we white man we d only with white woman 
 like ourselves . your maiden be fair , but they be not for we ! " 

 the king laugh . " it be well . in our land there be a proverb which 
 run , ' woman 's eye be always bright , whatever the colour , ' and 
 another that say , ' love she who be present , for be sure she who be 
 absent be false to thee ; ' but perhaps these thing be not so in the 
 star . in a land where man be white all thing be possible . so be it , 
 white man ; the girl will not go beg ! welcome again ; and welcome , 
 too , thou black one ; if Gagool here have win her way , thou wouldst have 
 be stiff and cold by now . it be lucky for thee that thou too camest 
 from the Stars ; ha ! ha ! " 

 " I can kill thee before thou killest I , o king , " be Ignosi 's calm 
 answer , " and thou shalt be stiff before my limb cease to bend . " 

 Twala start . " Thou speakest boldly , boy , " he reply angrily ; 
 " presume not too far . " 

 " he may well be bold in whose lip be truth . the truth be a sharp 
 spear which fly home and miss not . it be a message from ' the 
 star , ' o king . " 

 Twala scowl , and his one eye gleam fiercely , but he say nothing 
 more . 

 " let the dance begin , " he cry , and then the flower - crown girl 
 spring forward in company , sing a sweet song and wave the 
 delicate palm and white lily . on they dance , look faint and 
 spiritual in the soft , sad light of the risen moon ; now whirl round 
 and round , now meet in mimic warfare , sway , eddy here and 
 there , come forward , fall back in an order confusion delightful 
 to witness . at last they pause , and a beautiful young woman spring out

 vigour which would have put most ballet girl to shame . at length she 
 retire exhaust , and another take her place , then another and 
 another , but none of they , either in grace , skill , or personal 
 attraction , come up to the first . 

 when the choose girl have all dance , the king lift his hand . 

 " which deem ye the fairest , white man ? " he ask . 

 " the first , " say I unthinkingly . next second I regret it , for I 
 remember that Infadoos have tell we that the fair woman must be 
 offer up as a sacrifice . 

 " then be my mind as your mind , and my eye as your eye . she be the

 " ay , must die ! " pip out Gagool , cast a glance of her quick eye

 Twala laugh as he answer -

 maiden , to the Old Ones who sit and watch on the mountain , then shall

 make sharp thy spear . " 

 two of the man step forward , and as they advance , the girl , for the

 " what be thy name , girl ? " pip Gagool . " what ! wilt thou not answer ? 
 shall the king 's son do his work at once ? " 

 at this hint , Scragga , look more evil than ever , advance a step and

 " see , " cry Scragga in high glee , ' she shrink from the sight of my

 " if ever I get the chance you shall pay for that , you young hound ! " I 
 hear good mutter beneath his breath . 

 " now that thou art quiet , give we thy name , my dear . come , speak out , 
 and fear not , " say Gagool in mockery . 

 " oh , mother , " answer the girl , in tremble accent , " my name be 
 Foulata , of the house of Suko . oh , mother , why must I die ? I have do 
 no wrong ! " 

 " be comfort , " go on the old woman in her hateful tone of mockery . 
 " Thou must die , indeed , as a sacrifice to the Old Ones who sit yonder , " 
 and she point to the peak ; " but it be well to sleep in the night 
 than to toil in the daytime ; it be well to die than to live , and thou 
 shalt die by the royal hand of the king 's own son . " 

 the girl Foulata wring her hand in anguish , and cry out aloud , " oh , 
 cruel ! and I so young ! what have I do that I should never again see

 in the evening , that I may no more gather the flower when the dew be 
 heavy , or listen to the laughing of the water ? Woe be I , that I shall

 the lamb that be sick ! woe be I , that no lover shall put his arm 
 around I and look into my eye , nor shall man child be bear of I ! 
 oh , cruel , cruel ! " 

 and again she wring her hand and turn her tear - stain 
 flower - crown face to Heaven , look so lovely in her despair - for 
 she be indeed a beautiful woman - that assuredly the sight of she would 
 have melt the heart of any less cruel than be the three fiend 
 before we . Prince Arthur 's appeal to the ruffian who come to blind he 
 be not more touching than that of this savage girl . 

 but it do not move Gagool or Gagool 's master , though I see sign of

 " oh , white father from the star ! " she cry , " throw over I the mantle 
 of thy protection ; let I creep into the shadow of thy strength , that I

 Gagool ! " 

 " all right , my hearty , I will look after you , " sing out Good in nervous 
 Saxon . " come , get up , there be a good girl , " and he stoop and catch

 Twala turn and motion to his son , who advance with his spear 
 lift . 

 " now be your time , " whisper Sir Henry to I ; " what be you wait 
 for ? " 

 " I be wait for that eclipse , " I answer ; " I have have my eye on the 
 moon for the last half - hour , and I never see it look healthy . " 

 " well , you must risk it now , or the girl will be kill . Twala be 
 lose patience . " 

 recognise the force of the argument , and have cast one more

 ardent astronomer with a theory to prove await a celestial event with

 " king , " I say , " it shall not be ; we will not endure this thing ; let 
 the girl go in safety . " 

 Twala rise from his seat in wrath and astonishment , and from the chief 
 and serrie rank of maiden who have close in slowly upon we in 
 anticipation of the tragedy come a murmur of amazement . 

 " shall not be ! thou white dog , that yappest at the lion in his cave ; 
  shall not be ! art thou mad ? be careful , lest this chicken 's fate 
 overtake thee , and those with thee . how canst thou save she or thyself ? 
 who art thou that thou sett thyself between I and my will ? back , I 
 say . Scragga , kill she ! ho , guard ! seize these man . " 

 at his cry armed man run swiftly from behind the hut , where they have 
 evidently be place beforehand . 

 Sir Henry , Good , and Umbopa range themselves alongside of I , and 
 lift their rifle . 

 " stop ! " I shout boldly , though at the moment my heart be in my 
 boot . " stop ! we , the white man from the star , say that it shall not

 wind - blow lamp , as we who dwell in her House can do , and plunge the

 my threat produce an effect ; the man halt , and Scragga stand still

 " hear he ! hear he ! " pip Gagool ; " hear the liar who say that he 
 will put out the moon like a lamp . let he do it , and the girl shall be 
 spear . yes , let he do it , or die by the girl , he and those with he . " 

 I glance up at the moon despairingly , and now to my intense joy and 
 relief see that we - or rather the almanack - have make no mistake . on the 
 edge of the great orb lie a faint rim of shadow , while a smoky hue grow 
 and gather upon its bright surface . never shall I forget that 
 supreme , that superb moment of relief . 

 then I lift my hand solemnly towards the sky , an example which Sir 
 Henry and Good follow , and quote a line or two from the " Ingoldsby 
 legend " at it in the most impressive tone that I could command . Sir 
 Henry follow suit with a verse out of the Old Testament , and 
 something about Balbus build a wall , in Latin , whilst Good address 
 the queen of Night in a volume of the most classical bad language which 
 he could think of . 

 slowly the penumbra , the shadow of a shadow , creep on over the bright 
 surface , and as it creep I hear deep gasp of fear rise from the 
 multitude around . 

 " look , o king ! " I cry ; " look , Gagool ! look , chief and people and 
 woman , and see if the white man from the Stars keep their word , or if 
 they be but empty liar ! 

 " the moon grow black before your eye ; soon there will be 
 darkness - ay , darkness in the hour of the full moon . Ye have ask for 
 a sign ; it be give to you . grow dark , o Moon ! withdraw thy light , thou 
 pure and holy one ; bring the proud heart of usurping murderer to the 
 dust , and eat up the world with shadow . " 

 a groan of terror burst from the onlooker . some stand petrify with 
 dread , other throw themselves upon their knee and cry aloud . as for 
 the king , he sit still and turn pale beneath his dusky skin . only 
 Gagool keep her courage . 

 " it will pass , " she cry ; " I have often see the like before ; no man 
 can put out the moon ; lose not heart ; sit still - the shadow will pass . " 

 " wait , and ye shall see , " I reply , hop with excitement . " o moon ! 
 Moon ! moon ! wherefore art thou so cold and fickle ? " this appropriate 
 quotation be from the page of a popular romance that I chance to 
 have read recently , though now I come to think of it , it be ungrateful 
 of I to abuse the Lady of the Heavens , who be show herself to be 
 the truest of friend to we , however she may have behave to the 
 impassioned lover in the novel . then I add : " keep it up , good , I 
 can not   remember any more poetry . curse away , there be a good fellow . " 

 Good respond nobly to this tax upon his inventive faculty . never 
 before have I the faint conception of the breadth and depth and 
 height of a naval officer 's objurgatory power . for ten minute he go 
 on in several language without stop , and he scarcely ever repeat 
 himself . 

 meanwhile the dark ring creep on , while all that great assembly fix 
 their eye upon the sky and star and star in fascinated silence . 
 strange and unholy shadow encroach upon the moonlight , an ominous 
 quiet fill the place . everything grow still as death . slowly and in 
 the midst of this most solemn silence the minute speed away , and while 
 they speed the full moon pass deeply and deep into the shadow of the

 on , yet on , creep the ring of darkness ; it be now more than half 
 across the blood - red orb . the air grow thick , and still more deeply 
 ting with dusky crimson . on , yet on , till we could scarcely see the 
 fierce face of the group before we . no sound rise now from the 
 spectator , and at last Good stop swear . 

 " the moon be die - the white wizard have kill the moon , " yell the 
 prince Scragga at last . " we shall all perish in the dark , " and animate 
 by fear or fury , or by both , he lift his spear and drive it with all

 king have give we , and which we wear beneath our clothing . the steel 
 rebounded harmless , and before he could repeat the blow Curtis have 
 snatch the spear from his hand and send it straight through he . 

 Scragga drop dead . 

 at the sight , and drive mad with fear of the gathering darkness , and 
 of the unholy shadow which , as they believe , be swallow the moon ,

 Twala 's son . 

 " Chiefs , " I say , " we have give you the sign . if ye be satisfied , let 
 we fly swiftly to the place of which ye speak . the charm can not now be 
 stop . it will work for an hour and the half of an hour . let we cover

 " come , " say Infadoos , turn to go , an example which be follow by 
 the awed captain , ourselves , and the girl Foulata , whom Good take by 
 the arm . 

 before we reach the gate of the kraal the moon go out utterly , and 
 from every quarter of the firmament the star rush forth into the 
 inky sky . 

 hold each other by the hand we stumble on through the darkness . 



 CHAPTER XII 

 before the battle 

 luckily for we , Infadoos and the chief know all the path of the great 
 town perfectly , so that we pass by side - way unmoleste , and 
 notwithstanding the gloom we make fair progress . 

 for an hour or more we journey on , till at length the eclipse begin 
 to pass , and that edge of the moon which have disappear the first 
 become again visible . suddenly , as we watch , there burst from it a 
 silver streak of light , accompany by a wondrous ruddy glow , which 
 hang upon the blackness of the sky like a celestial lamp , and a wild 
 and lovely sight it be . in another five minute the star begin to 
 fade , and there be sufficient light to see our whereabouts . we then 
 discover that we be clear of the town of Loo , and approach a 
 large flat - top hill , measure some two mile in circumference . this 
 hill , which be of a formation common in South Africa , be not very high ; 
 indeed , its great elevation be scarcely more than 200 foot , but it 
 be shape like a horseshoe , and its side be rather precipitous and 
 strew with boulder . on the grass table - land at its summit be ample 
 camping - ground , which have be utilise as a military cantonment of no 
 mean strength . its ordinary garrison be one regiment of three thousand 
 man , but as we toil up the steep side of the mountain in the 
 return moonlight we perceive that there be several of such 
 regiment encamp there . 

 reach the table - land at last , we find crowd of man rouse from 
 their sleep , shiver with fear and huddle up together in the utmost 
 consternation at the natural phenomenon which they be witness . 
 pass through these without a word , we gain a hut in the centre of 
 the ground , where we be astonish to find two man wait , laden 
 with our few good and chattel , which of course we have be oblige to 
 leave behind in our hasty flight . 

 " I send for they , " explain Infadoos ; " and also for these , " and he 
 lift up Good 's long - lose trouser . 

 with an exclamation of rapturous delight Good spring at they , and 
 instantly proceed to put they on . 

 " surely my lord will not hide his beautiful white leg ! " exclaim 
 infadoo regretfully . 

 but Good persist , and once only do the Kukuana people get the chance 
 of see his beautiful leg again . good be a very modest man . 
 Henceforward they have to satisfy their æsthetic longing with his one 
 whisker , his transparent eye , and his movable tooth . 

 still gaze with fond remembrance at Good 's trouser , Infadoos next 
 inform we that he have command the regiment to muster so soon as 
 the day break , in order to explain to they fully the origin and 
 circumstance of the rebellion which be decide on by the chief , and 
 to introduce to they the rightful heir to the throne , Ignosi . 

 accordingly , when the sun be up , the troop - in all some twenty 
 thousand man , and the flower of the Kukuana army - be muster on a 
 large open space , to which we go . the man be draw up in three 
 side of a dense square , and present a magnificent spectacle . we take 
 our station on the open side of the square , and be speedily 
 surround by all the principal chief and officer . 

 these , after silence have be proclaim , Infadoos proceed to 
 address . he narrate to they in vigorous and graceful language - for , 
 like most Kukuanas of high rank , he be a bear orator - the history of 
 Ignosi 's father , and of how he have be basely murder by Twala the 
 king , and his wife and child drive out to starve . then he point out 
 that the people suffer and groan under Twala 's cruel rule , 
 instance the proceeding of the previous night , when , under pretence 
 of their be evil - doer , many of the noblest in the land have be 
 drag forth and wickedly do to death . next he go on to say that 
 the white lord from the star , look down upon their country , have 
 perceive its trouble , and determine , at great personal inconvenience , 
 to alleviate its lot : that they have accordingly take the real king of 
 the Kukuanas , Ignosi , who be languish in exile , by the hand , and 
 lead he over the mountain : that they have see the wickedness of 
 Twala 's doing , and for a sign to the wavering , and to save the life of 
 the girl Foulata , actually , by the exercise of their high magic , have 
 put out the moon and slay the young fiend Scragga ; and that they be 
 prepared to stand by they , and assist they to overthrow Twala , and set 
 up the rightful king , Ignosi , in his place . 

 he finish his discourse amidst a murmur of approbation . then Ignosi 
 step forward and begin to speak . have reiterate all that Infadoos 
 his uncle have say , he conclude a powerful speech in these word : - 

 " O chief , captain , soldier , and people , ye have hear my word . now 
 must ye make choice between I and he who sit upon my throne , the 
 uncle who kill his brother , and hunt his brother 's child forth to 
 die in the cold and the night . that I be indeed the king 
 these " - point to the chiefs - " can tell you , for they have see the 
 snake about my middle . if I be not the king , would these white man be 
 on my side with all their magic ? tremble , chief , captain , soldier , 
 and people ! be not the darkness they have bring upon the land to 
 confound Twala and cover our flight , darkness even in the hour of the 
 full moon , yet before your eye ? " 

 " it be , " answer the soldier . 

 " I be the king ; I say to you , I be the king , " go on Ignosi , draw 
 up his great stature to its full , and lift his broad - blade 
 battle - axe above his head . " if there be any man among you who say that 
 it be not so , let he stand forth and I will fight he now , and his 
 blood shall be a red token that I tell you true . let he stand forth , I 
 say ; " and he shake the great axe till it flash in the sunlight . 

 as nobody seem inclined to respond to this heroic version of " dilly , 
 dilly , come and be kill , " our late henchman proceed with his 
 address . 

 " I be indeed the king , and should ye stand by my side in the battle , if 
 I win the day ye shall go with I to victory and honour . I will give 
 you oxen and wife , and ye shall take place of all the regiment ; and 
 if ye fall , I will fall with you . 

 " and behold , I give you this promise , that when I sit upon the seat of 
 my father , bloodshed shall cease in the land . no long shall ye cry 
 for justice to find slaughter , no long shall the witch - finder hunt 
 you out so that ye may be slay without a cause . no man shall die save 
 he who offend against the law . the ' eat up ' of your kraal shall 
 cease ; each one of you shall sleep secure in his own hut and fear 
 naught , and justice shall walk blindfold throughout the land . have ye 
 choose , chief , captain , soldier , and people ? " 

 " we have choose , o king , " come back the answer . 

 " it be well . turn your head and see how Twala 's messenger go forth 
 from the great town , east and west , and north and south , to gather a 
 mighty army to slay I and you , and these my friend and protector . 
 to - morrow , or perchance the next day , he will come against we with all 
 who be faithful to he . then I shall see the man who be indeed my man , 
 the man who fear not to die for his cause ; and I tell you that he 
 shall not be forget in the time of spoil . I have speak , O chief , 
 captain , soldier , and people . now go to your hut and make you ready 
 for war . " 

 there be a pause , till presently one of the chief lift his hand , 
 and out roll the royal salute , " Koom . " it be a sign that the 
 soldier accept Ignosi as their king . then they march off in 
 battalion . 

 half an hour afterwards we hold a council of war , at which all the 
 commander of regiment be present . it be evident to we that before 
 very long we should be attack in overwhelming force . indeed , from our 
 point of vantage on the hill we could see troop muster , and runner 
 go forth from Loo in every direction , doubtless to summon soldier 
 to the king 's assistance . we have on our side about twenty thousand man , 
 compose of seven of the good regiment in the country . Twala , so 
 Infadoos and the chief calculate , have at least thirty to thirty - five 
 thousand on whom he could rely at present assemble in Loo , and they 
 think that by midday on the morrow he would be able to gather another 
 five thousand or more to his aid . it be , of course , possible that some 
 of his troop would desert and come over to we , but it be not a 
 contingency which could be reckon on . meanwhile , it be clear that 
 active preparation be be make by Twala to subdue we . already 
 strong body of armed man be patrol round and round the foot of 
 the hill , and there be other sign also of come assault . 

 Infadoos and the chief , however , be of opinion that no attack would 
 take place that day , which would be devoted to preparation and to the 
 removal of every available mean of the moral effect produce upon the 
 mind of the soldiery by the suppose magical darkening of the moon . 
 the onslaught would be on the morrow , they say , and they prove to be 
 right . 

 meanwhile , we set to work to strengthen the position in all way 
 possible . almost every man be turn out , and in the course of the 
 day , which seem far too short , much be do . the path up the 
 hill - that be rather a sanatorium than a fortress , be use 
 generally as the camping place of regiment suffer from recent 
 service in unhealthy portion of the country - be carefully block 
 with mass of stone , and every other approach be make as impregnable 
 as time would allow . pile of boulder be collect at various spot 
 to be roll down upon an advance enemy , station be appoint to 
 the different regiment , and all preparation be make which our joint 
 ingenuity could suggest . 

 just before sundown , as we rest after our toil , we perceive a small 
 company of man advance towards we from the direction of Loo , one of 
 whom bear a palm leaf in his hand for a sign that he come as a herald . 

 as he draw near , Ignosi , Infadoos , one or two chief and ourselves , 
 go down to the foot of the mountain to meet he . he be a 
 gallant - look fellow , wear the regulation leopard - skin cloak . 

 " greet ! " he cry , as he come ; " the king 's greeting to those who 
 make unholy war against the king ; the lion 's greeting to the jackal 
 that snarl around his heel . " 

 " speak , " I say . 

 " these be the king 's word . surrender to the king 's mercy ere a bad 
 thing befall you . already the shoulder have be tear from the black 
 bull , and the king drive he bleed about the camp . " 1 

 " what be Twala 's term ? " I ask from curiosity . 

 " his term be merciful , worthy of a great king . these be the word of 
 Twala , the one - eye , the mighty , the husband of a thousand wife , lord 
 of the Kukuanas , keeper of the Great Road   Solomon 's Road , belove of 
 the Strange Ones who sit in silence at the mountain yonder   the Three 
 Witches , Calf of the black Cow , Elephant whose tread shake the earth , 
 Terror of the evil - doer , Ostrich whose foot devour the desert , huge 
 one , black one , wise one , king from generation to generation ! these be 
 the word of Twala : ' I will have mercy and be satisfied with a little 
 blood . one in every ten shall die , the rest shall go free ; but the 
 white man Incubu , who slay Scragga my son , and the black man his 
 servant , who pretend to my throne , and Infadoos my brother , who brew 
 rebellion against I , these shall die by torture as an offering to the 
 Silent Ones . ' such be the merciful word of Twala . " 

 after consult with the other a little , I answer he in a loud 
 voice , so that the soldier might hear , thus - 

 " go back , thou dog , to Twala , who send thee , and say that we , Ignosi , 
 veritable king of the Kukuanas , Incubu , Bougwan , and Macumazahn , the 
 wise one from the Stars , who make dark the moon , Infadoos , of the 
 royal house , and the chief , captain , and people here gather , make 
 answer and say , ' that we will not surrender ; that before the sun have 
 go down twice , Twala 's corpse shall stiffen at Twala 's gate , and

 the herald laugh loudly . " ye frighten not man with such swell

 the moonlight flicker along their spear , play upon their feature

 " how many of these do you suppose will be alive at this time

 touch they . my mind 's eye single out those who be seal to

 mystery of human life , and an overwhelming sorrow at its futility and 
 sadness . to - night these thousand sleep their healthy sleep , to - morrow 
 they , and many other with they , ourselves perhaps among they , would be 
 stiffening in the cold ; their wife would be widow , their child 
 fatherless , and their place know they no more for ever . only the old 
 moon would shine on serenely , the night wind would stir the grass , 
 and the wide earth would take its rest , even as it do æon before we 
 be , and will do æon after we have be forget . 

 yet man die not whilst the world , at once his mother and his monument , 
 remain . his name be lose , indeed , but the breath he breathe still 
 stir the pine - top on the mountain , the sound of the word he speak 
 yet echo on through space ; the thought his brain give birth to we 
 have inherit to - day ; his passion be our cause of life ; the joy and 
 sorrow that he know be our familiar friend - the end from which he 
 flee aghast will surely overtake we also ! 

 truly the universe be full of ghost , not sheet churchyard spectre , 
 but the inextinguishable element of individual life , which have once 
 be , can never die , though they blend and change , and change again 
 for ever . 


 all sort of reflection of this nature pass through my mind - for as

  1   this cruel custom be not confine to the Kukuanas , but be by no 
 mean uncommon amongst african tribe on the occasion of the outbreak

 CHAPTER XIII 

 the ATTACK

 " good ; it be now mid - day , and the man eat and rest after the toil of

 CHAPTER XIV 

 the last stand of the greys 

 in a few more minute the regiment destine to carry out the flanking 
 movement have tramp off in silence , keep carefully to the lee of 
 the rise ground in order to conceal their advance from the keen eye 
 of Twala 's scout . 

 half an hour or more be allow to elapse between the setting out of 
 the horn or wing of the army before any stir be make by the Greys 
 and their support regiment , know as the Buffaloes , which form its 
 chest , and be destine to bear the brunt of the battle . 

 both of these regiment be almost perfectly fresh , and of full 
 strength , the Greys have be in reserve in the morning , and have

 Infadoos , who be a wary old general , and know the absolute importance

 Greys , in poetical language : explain to they the honour that they 
 be receive in be put thus in the forefront of the battle , and in

 I look down the long line of wave black plume and stern face 
 beneath they , and sigh to think that within one short hour most , if 
 not all , of those magnificent veteran warrior , not a man of whom be 
 under forty year of age , would be lay dead or die in the dust . it 
 could not be otherwise ; they be be condemn , with that wise

 save his force and attain his end , to certain slaughter , in order 
 to give their cause and the remainder of the army a chance of success . 
 they be foredoom to die , and they know the truth . it be to be 
 their task to engage regiment after regiment of Twala 's army on the 
 narrow strip of green beneath we , till they be exterminate or till 
 the wing find a favourable opportunity for their onslaught . and yet 
 they never hesitate , nor could I detect a sign of fear upon the face 
 of a single warrior . there they be - go to certain death , about to 
 quit the blessed light of day for ever , and yet able to contemplate 
 their doom without a tremor . even at that moment I could not help 
 contrast their state of mind with my own , which be far from 
 comfortable , and breathe a sigh of envy and admiration . never before 
 have I see such an absolute devotion to the idea of duty , and such a 
 complete indifference to its bitter fruit . 

 " behold your king ! " end old Infadoos , point to Ignosi ; " go fight 
 and fall for he , as be the duty of brave man , and curse and shameful 
 for ever be the name of he who shrink from death for his king , or who 
 turn his back to the foe . behold your king , chief , captain , and 
 soldier ! now do your homage to the sacred Snake , and then follow on , 
 that Incubu and I may show you a road to the heart of Twala 's host . " 

 there be a moment 's pause , then suddenly a murmur arise from the 
 serrie phalanx before we , a sound like the distant whisper of the 
 sea , cause by the gentle tap of the handle of six thousand spear 
 against their holder ' shield . slowly it swell , till its grow 
 volume deepen and widen into a roar of rolling noise , that echo

 CHAPTER XV 

 good FALLS SICK 

 after the fight be end , Sir Henry and Good be carry into Twala 's

 be very wiry , and can stand more fatigue than most man , probably on

  " of farewell to the dying 
  and mourning for the dead . "

 CHAPTER XVI 

 the PLACE of DEATH 

 it be already dark on the third day after the scene describe in the 
 previous chapter when we camp in some hut at the foot of the " Three 
 Witches , " as the triangle of mountain be call to which Solomon 's 
 Great Road run . our party consist of our three self and Foulata , 
 who wait on we - especially on Good - Infadoos , Gagool , who be bear 
 along in a litter , inside which she could be hear mutter and 
 curse all day long , and a party of guard and attendant . the 
 mountain , or rather the three peak of the mountain , for the mass be 
 evidently the result of a solitary upheaval , be , as I have say , in 
 the form of a triangle , of which the base be towards we , one peak 
 be on our right , one on our left , and one straight in front of we . 
 never shall I forget the sight afford by those three tower peak 
 in the early sunlight of the following morning . high , high above we , up

 that run up the slope towards they . straight before we the white 
 ribbon of Solomon 's Great Road stretch away uphill to the foot of the 
 centre peak , about five mile from we , and there stop . it be its 
 terminus . 

 I have well leave the feeling of intense excitement with which we set 
 out on our march that morning to the imagination of those who read this 
 history . at last we be draw near to the wonderful mine that have 
 be the cause of the miserable death of the old Portuguese Dom three 
 century ago , of my poor friend , his ill - star descendant , and also ,

 they , as that old fiend Gagool say ; would it also befall we ? somehow ,

 do Good and Sir Henry . 

 for an hour and a half or more we tramp on up the heather - fringe

 " walk more slowly , white man , " she say , project her hideous

 however , on we go , till we see before we , and between ourselves and 
 the peak , a vast circular hole with slop side , three hundred foot 
 or more in depth , and quite half a mile round . 

 " can not   you guess what this be ? " I say to Sir Henry and Good , who be 
 star in astonishment at the awful pit before we . 

 they shake their head . 

 " then it be clear that you have never see the diamond digging at 
 Kimberley . you may depend on it that this be Solomon 's Diamond Mine .

 at the edge of this vast hole , which be none other than the pit mark

 it . in many place , by the way , this surround road be build

 great gulf . as we draw near we perceive that they be Colossi of some 
 sort or another , and rightly conjecture that before we sit the three 
 " Silent Ones " that be hold in such awe by the Kukuana people . but it 
 be not until we be quite close to they that we recognise the full 
 majesty of these " Silent Ones . " 

 there , upon huge pedestal of dark rock , sculpture with rude emblem 
 of the Phallic worship , separate from each other by a distance of 
 forty pace , and look down the road which cross some sixty mile 
 of plain to Loo , be three colossal seat form - two male and one 
 female - each measure about thirty foot from the crown of its head to

 the female form , which be nude , be of great though severe beauty , but 
 unfortunately the feature have be injure by century of exposure to

 contemplate these " Silent Ones , " as the Kukuanas call they , an 
 intense curiosity again seize we to know whose be the hand which 
 have shape they , who it be that have dig the pit and make the road . 
 whilst I be gaze and wonder , suddenly it occur to I - be 
 familiar with the Old Testament - that Solomon go astray after strange

 of the Zidonians , Chemosh , the god of the Moabites , and Milcom , the god 
 of the child of Ammon " - and I suggest to my companion that the 
 figure before we might represent these false and exploded divinity . 

 " Hum , " say Sir Henry , who be a scholar , have take a high degree in

 " then give I the basket . "

 " the deuce you will ! " think I to myself ; " that may be rather awkward

 let the reader picture to himself the hall of the vast cathedral he

 even as we gaze we could hear the process go on , for presently with

 take to form a pillar , say eighty foot by ten in diameter . that the 
 process , in at least one instance , be incalculably slow , the follow

 to be the figure of an egyptian god , doubtless the handiwork of some

 ground . yet at the time that we see it , which must have be nearly

 or an inch and a fraction to a century . this we know because , as we 
 be stand by it , we hear a drop of water fall . 

 sometimes the stalagmite take strange form , presumably where the

 anything more awe - inspiring than the spectacle of this long line of

 my own idea be , that this terrific object be a freak of fancy on the

 all I can do be to describe it as it be , and the reader must form his

 such , at any rate , be the White Death and such be the White Dead !

 we ABANDON HOPE

 CHAPTER XIX 

 IGNOSI 's FAREWELL 

 ten day from that eventful morning find we once more in our old

 remain , include ninety - three large stone range from over two

 on arrive at Loo we be most cordially receive by Ignosi , whom we

 " ay , my lord the king ! Thy father 's father and I be bear on the same

 " go ! "

 between ourselves that I should , I take the opportunity to address 
 Ignosi as to our departure from Kukuanaland . 

 " and now , Ignosi , " I say , " the time have come for we to bid thee 
 farewell , and start to see our own land once more . Behold , Ignosi , thou 
 camest with we a servant , and now we leave thee a mighty king . if thou 
 art grateful to we , remember to do even as thou didst promise : to rule 
 justly , to respect the law , and to put none to death without a cause . 
 so shalt thou prosper . to - morrow , at break of day , Ignosi , thou wilt 
 give we an escort who shall lead we across the mountain . be it not so , 
 o king ? " 

 Ignosi cover his face with his hand for a while before answer . 

 " my heart be sore , " he say at last ; " your word split my heart in 
 twain . what have I do to you , Incubu , Macumazahn , and Bougwan , that 
 ye should leave I desolate ? Ye who stand by I in rebellion and in 
 battle , will ye leave I in the day of peace and victory ? what will 
 ye - wife ? choose from among the maiden ! a place to live in ? Behold , 
 the land be yours as far as ye can see . the white man 's house ? ye 
 shall teach my people how to build they . Cattle for beef and milk ? 
 every married man shall bring you an ox or a cow . wild game to hunt ? 
 do not the elephant walk through my forest , and the river - horse 
 sleep in the reed ? would ye make war ? my Impis wait your word . if 
 there be anything more which I can give , that will I give you . " 

 " Nay , Ignosi , we want none of these thing , " I answer ; " we would seek 
 our own place . " 

 " now do I learn , " say Ignosi bitterly , and with flash eye , " that 
 ye love the bright stone more than I , your friend . ye have the 
 stone ; now ye would go to Natal and across the move black water and 
 sell they , and be rich , as it be the desire of a white man 's heart to 
 be . curse for your sake be the white stone , and curse he who seek 
 they . death shall it be to he who set foot in the place of Death to 
 find they . I have speak . white man , ye can go . " 

 I lay my hand upon his arm . " Ignosi , " I say , " tell we , when thou 
 didst wander in Zululand , and among the white people of Natal , do not 
 thine heart turn to the land thy mother tell thee of , thy native place , 
 where thou didst see the light , and play when thou wast little , the 
 land where thy place be ? " 

 " it be even so , Macumazahn . " 

 " in like manner , Ignosi , do our heart turn to our land and to our own 
 place . " 

 then come a silence . when Ignosi break it , it be in a different voice . 

 " I do perceive that now as ever thy word be wise and full of reason , 
 Macumazahn ; that which fly in the air love not to run along the 
 ground ; the white man love not to live on the level of the black or to 
 house among his kraal . well , ye must go , and leave my heart sore , 
 because ye will be as dead to I , since from where ye be no tiding 
 can come to I . 

 " but listen , and let all your brother know my word . no other white 
 man shall cross the mountain , even if any man live to come so far . I 
 will see no trader with their gun and gin . my people shall fight with 
 the spear , and drink water , like their forefather before they . I will 
 have no pray - man to put a fear of death into man 's heart , to stir 
 they up against the law of the king , and make a path for the white folk 
 who follow to run on . if a white man come to my gate I will send he 
 back ; if a hundred come I will push they back ; if army come , I will 
 make war on they with all my strength , and they shall not prevail 
 against I . none shall ever seek for the shin stone : no , not an 
 army , for if they come I will send a regiment and fill up the pit , and 
 break down the white column in the cave and choke they with rock , so 
 that none can reach even to that door of which ye speak , and whereof 
 the way to move it be lose . but for you three , Incubu , Macumazahn , and 
 Bougwan , the path be always open ; for , behold , ye be dearer to I than 
 aught that breathe . 

 " and ye would go . infadoo , my uncle , and my Induna , shall take you by 
 the hand and guide you with a regiment . there be , as I have learn , 
 another way across the mountain that he shall show you . farewell , my 
 brother , brave white man . see I no more , for I have no heart to bear 
 it . Behold ! I make a decree , and it shall be publish from the 
 mountain to the mountain ; your name , Incubu , Macumazahn , and 
 Bougwan , shall be " hlonipa " even as the name of dead king , and he 
 who speak they shall die . 1   so shall your memory be preserve in the 
 land for ever . 

 " go now , ere my eye rain tear like a woman 's . at time as ye look 
 back down the path of life , or when ye be old and gather yourself 
 together to crouch before the fire , because for you the sun have no more 
 heat , ye will think of how we stand shoulder to shoulder , in that great 
 battle which thy wise word plan , Macumazahn ; of how thou wast the 
 point of the horn that gall Twala 's flank , Bougwan ; whilst thou stand 
 in the ring of the Greys , Incubu , and man go down before thine axe 
 like corn before a sickle ; ay , and of how thou didst break that wild 
 bull Twala 's strength , and bring his pride to dust . fare ye well for 
 ever , Incubu , Macumazahn , and Bougwan , my lord and my friend . " 

 Ignosi rise and look earnestly at we for a few second . then he throw 
 the corner of his karross over his head , so as to cover his face from 
 we . 

 we go in silence . 


 next day at dawn we leave Loo , escort by our old friend Infadoos , who 
 be heart - break at our departure , and by the regiment of Buffaloes . 
 early as be the hour , all the main street of the town be line with 
 multitude of people , who give we the royal salute as we pass at the 
 head of the regiment , while the woman bless we for have rid the 
 land of Twala , throw flower before we as we go . it be really 
 very affect , and not the sort of thing one be accustom to meet 
 with from native . 

 one ludicrous incident occur , however , which I rather welcome , as 
 it give we something to laugh at . 

 just before we reach the confine of the town , a pretty young girl , 
 with some lovely lily in her hand , run forward and present they to 
 Good - somehow they all seem to like Good ; I think his eye - glass and 
 solitary whisker give he a fictitious value - and then say that she 
 have a boon to ask . 

 " speak on , " he answer . 

 " let my lord show his servant his beautiful white leg , that his 
 servant may look upon they , and remember they all her day , and tell of 
 they to her child ; his servant have travel four day ' journey to 
 see they , for the fame of they have go throughout the land . " 

 " I will be hang if I do ! " exclaim Good excitedly . 

 " come , come , my dear fellow , " say Sir Henry , " you can not   refuse to 
 oblige a lady . " 

 " I will not , " reply Good obstinately ; " it be positively indecent . " 

 however , in the end he consent to draw up his trouser to the knee , 
 amidst note of rapturous admiration from all the woman present , 
 especially the gratified young lady , and in this guise he have to walk 
 till we get clear of the town . 

 Good 's leg , I fear , will never be so greatly admire again . of his 
 melting tooth , and even of his " transparent eye , " the Kukuanas weary 
 more or less , but of his leg never . 

 as we travel , Infadoos tell we that there be another pass over the 
 mountain to the north of the one follow by Solomon 's Great Road , or 
 rather that there be a place where it be possible to climb down the 
 wall of cliff which separate Kukuanaland from the desert , and be 
 break by the tower shape of Sheba 's Breasts . it appear , also , 
 that rather more than two year previously a party of Kukuana hunter 
 have descend this path into the desert in search of ostrich , whose 
 plume be much prize among they for war head - dress , and that in the 
 course of their hunt they have be lead far from the mountain and be 
 much trouble by thirst . see tree on the horizon , however , they 
 walk towards they , and discover a large and fertile oasis some 
 mile in extent , and plentifully water . it be by way of this oasis 
 that Infadoos suggest we should return , and the idea seem to we a 
 good one , for it appear that we should thus escape the rigour of the 
 mountain pass . also some of the hunter be in attendance to guide we 
 to the oasis , from which , they state , they could perceive other 
 fertile spot far away in the desert . 2 

 travel easily , on the night of the fourth day 's journey we find 
 ourselves once more on the crest of the mountain that separate 
 Kukuanaland from the desert , which roll away in sandy billow at our 
 foot , and about twenty - five mile to the north of Sheba 's Breasts . 

 at dawn on the follow day , we be lead to the edge of a very 
 precipitous chasm , by which we be to descend the precipice , and gain 
 the plain two thousand and more foot below . 

 here we bade farewell to that true friend and sturdy old warrior , 
 Infadoos , who solemnly wish all good upon we , and nearly weep with 
 grief . " never , my lord , " he say , ' shall mine old eye see the like of 
 you again . ah ! the way that Incubu cut his man down in the battle ! ah ! 
 for the sight of that stroke with which he sweep off my brother Twala 's 
 head ! it be beautiful - beautiful ! I may never hope to see such 
 another , except perchance in happy dream . " 

 we be very sorry to part from he ; indeed , Good be so moved that he 
 give he as a souvenir - what do you think ? - an eye - glass ; afterwards 
 we discover that it be a spare one . infadoo be delighted , 
 foresee that the possession of such an article would increase his 
 prestige enormously , and after several vain attempt he actually 
 succeed in screw it into his own eye . anything more incongruous 
 than the old warrior look with an eye - glass I never see . eye - glass 
 do not go well with leopard - skin cloak and black ostrich plume . 

 then , after see that our guide be well laden with water and 
 provision , and have receive a thunder farewell salute from the 
 Buffaloes , we wring Infadoos by the hand , and begin our downward climb . 
 a very arduous business it prove to be , but somehow that evening we 
 find ourselves at the bottom without accident . 

 " do you know , " say Sir Henry that night , as we sit by our fire and 
 gaze up at the beetle cliff above we , " I think that there be bad 
 place than Kukuanaland in the world , and that I have know unhappier 
 time than the last month or two , though I have never spend such queer 
 one . eh ! you fellow ? " 

 " I almost wish I be back , " say Good , with a sigh . 

 as for myself , I reflect that all be well that end well ; but in the 
 course of a long life of shave , I never have such shave as those which 
 I have recently experience . the thought of that battle make I feel 
 cold all over , and as for our experience in the treasure chamber - ! 


 next morning we start on a toilsome trudge across the desert , have 
 with we a good supply of water carry by our five guide , and camp 
 that night in the open , march again at dawn on the morrow . 

 by noon of the third day 's journey we could see the tree of the oasis 
 of which the guide speak , and within an hour of sundown we be 
 walk once more upon grass and listen to the sound of run 
 water . 


  1   this extraordinary and negative way of show intense respect be 
 by no mean unknown among african people , and the result be that if , as 
 be usual , the name in question have a significance , the meaning must be 
 express by an idiom or other word . in this way a memory be preserve 
 for generation , or until the new word utterly supplant the old . 

  2   it often puzzle all of we to understand how it be possible that 
 Ignosi 's mother , bear the child with she , should have survive the 
 danger of her journey across the mountain and the desert , danger 
 which so nearly prove fatal to ourselves . it have since occur to I , 
 and I give the idea to the reader for what it be worth , that she must 
 have take this second route , and wander out like Hagar into the 
 wilderness . if she do so , there be no long anything inexplicable 
 about the story , since , as Ignosi himself relate , she may well have 
 be pick up by some ostrich hunter before she or the child be 
 exhaust , be lead by they to the oasis , and thence by stage to the 
 fertile country , and so on by slow degree southward to Zululand . - A.Q. 



 CHAPTER XX 

 FOUND 

 and now I come to perhaps the strange adventure that happen to we 
 in all this strange business , and one which show how wonderfully 
 thing be bring about . 

 I be walk along quietly , some way in front of the other two , down 
 the bank of the stream which run from the oasis till it be swallow 
 up in the hungry desert sand , when suddenly I stop and rub my 
 eye , as well I might . there , not twenty yard in front of I , place 
 in a charming situation , under the shade of a species of fig - tree , and 
 face to the stream , be a cosy hut , build more or less on the Kafir 
 principle with grass and withe , but have a full - length door instead 
 of a bee - hole . 

 " what the dicken , " say I to myself , " can a hut be do here ? " even 
 as I say it the door of the hut open , and there limp out of it a 
  white man clothe in skin , and with an enormous black beard . I 
 think that I must have get a touch of the sun . it be impossible . no 
 hunter ever come to such a place as this . certainly no hunter would 
 ever settle in it . I star and star , and so do the other man , and 
 just at that juncture Sir Henry and Good walk up . 

 " look here , you fellow , " I say , " be that a white man , or be I mad ? " 

 Sir Henry look , and Good look , and then all of a sudden the lame 
 white man with a black beard utter a great cry , and begin hobble 
 towards we . when he be close he fall down in a sort of faint . 

 with a spring Sir Henry be by his side . 

 " Great Powers ! " he cry , " it be my brother George ! " 

 at the sound of this disturbance , another figure , also clothe in skin , 
 emerge from the hut , a gun in his hand , and run towards we . on see 
 I he too give a cry . 

 " Macumazahn , " he halloe , " do not   you know I , Baas ? I be Jim the hunter . 
 I lose the note you give I to give to the Baas , and we have be here 
 nearly two year . " and the fellow fall at my foot , and roll over and 
 over , weep for joy . 

 " you careless scoundrel ! " I say ; " you ought to be well 
  sjambocke " - that be , hide . 

 meanwhile the man with the black beard have recover and rise , and he 
 and Sir Henry be pump - handling away at each other , apparently without 
 a word to say . but whatever they have quarrel about in the past - I 
 suspect it be a lady , though I never ask - it be evidently forget 
 now . 

 " my dear old fellow , " burst out Sir Henry at last , " I think you be 
 dead . I have be over Solomon 's Mountains to find you . I have give up 
 all hope of ever see you again , and now I come across you perch in 
 the desert , like an old assv"gel . " 1 

 " I try to cross Solomon 's Mountains nearly two year ago , " be the 
 answer , speak in the hesitate voice of a man who have have little 
 recent opportunity of use his tongue , " but when I reach here a 
 boulder fall on my leg and crush it , and I have be able to go 
 neither forward nor back . " 

 then I come up . " how do you do , Mr. Neville ? " I say ; " do you remember 
 I ? " 

 " why , " he say , " be not   it Hunter Quatermain , eh , and Good too ? hold on 
 a minute , you fellow , I be get dizzy again . it be all so very 
 strange , and , when a man have cease to hope , so very happy ! " 

 that evening , over the camp fire , George Curtis tell we his story , 
 which , in its way , be almost as eventful as our own , and , put shortly , 
 amount to this . a little less than two year before , he have start 
 from Sitanda 's Kraal , to try to reach Suliman 's Berg . as for the note I 
 have send he by Jim , that worthy lose it , and he have never hear of it 
 till to - day . but , act upon information he have receive from the 
 native , he head not for Sheba 's Breasts , but for the ladder - like 
 descent of the mountain down which we have just come , which be clearly 
 a well route than that mark out in old Dom Silvestra 's plan . in the 
 desert he and Jim have suffer great hardship , but finally they 
 reach this oasis , where a terrible accident befell George Curtis . on 
 the day of their arrival he be sit by the stream , and Jim be 
 extract the honey from the nest of a stingless bee which be to be 
 find in the desert , on the top of a bank immediately above he . in so 
 do he loosen a great boulder of rock , which fall upon George 
 Curtis 's right leg , crush it frightfully . from that day he have be 
 so lame that he find it impossible to go either forward or back , and 
 have prefer to take the chance of die in the oasis to the 
 certainty of perish in the desert . 

 as for food , however , they get on pretty well , for they have a good 
 supply of ammunition , and the oasis be frequent , especially at 
 night , by large quantity of game , which come thither for water . these 
 they shoot , or trap in pitfall , use the flesh for food , and , after 
 their clothe wear out , the hide for clothing . 

 " and so , " George Curtis end , " we have live for nearly two year , 
 like a second Robinson Crusoe and his man Friday , hop against hope 
 that some native might come here to help we away , but none have come . 
 only last night we settle that Jim should leave I , and try to reach 
 Sitanda 's Kraal to get assistance . he be to go to - morrow , but I have 
 little hope of ever see he back again . and now you , of all people 
 in the world , you , who , as I fancy , have long ago forget all 
 about I , and be live comfortably in old England , turn up in a 
 promiscuous way and find I where you least expect . it be the most 
 wonderful thing that I have ever hear of , and the most merciful too . " 

 then Sir Henry set to work , and tell he the main fact of our 
 adventure , sit till late into the night to do it . 

 " by Jove ! " say George Curtis , when I show he some of the diamond : 
 " well , at least you have get something for your pain , besides my 
 worthless self . " 

 Sir Henry laugh . " they belong to Quatermain and Good . it be a part 
 of the bargain that they should divide any spoil there might be . " 

 this remark set I think , and have speak to Good , I tell Sir 
 Henry that it be our joint wish that he should take a third portion of 
 the diamond , or , if he would not , that his share should be hand to 
 his brother , who have suffer even more than ourselves on the chance of 
 get they . finally , we prevail upon he to consent to this 
 arrangement , but George Curtis do not know of it until some time 
 afterwards . 

          

 here , at this point , I think that I shall end my history . our journey 
 across the desert back to Sitanda 's Kraal be most arduous , especially 
 as we have to support George Curtis , whose right leg be very weak 
 indeed , and continually throw out splinter of bone . but we do 
 accomplish it somehow , and to give its detail would only be to 
 reproduce much of what happen to we on the former occasion . 

 six month from the date of our re - arrival at Sitanda 's , where we find 
 our gun and other good quite safe , though the old rascal in charge 
 be much disgusted at our survive to claim they , see we all once more 
 safe and sound at my little place on the Berea , near Durban , where I be 
 now write . Thence I bid farewell to all who have accompany I 
 through the strange trip I ever make in the course of a long and 
 varied experience . 

 P.S. - just as I have write the last word , a Kafir come up my avenue of 
 orange tree , carry a letter in a cleft stick , which he have bring 
 from the post . it turn out to be from Sir Henry , and as it speak for 
 itself I give it in full . 

  October 1 , 1884 . 
  Brayley Hall , Yorkshire . 

  my Dear Quatermain , 

  I send you a line a few mail back to say that the three of we , 
  George , Good , and myself , fetch up all right in England . we get 
  off the boat at Southampton , and go up to town . you should have 
  see what a swell Good turn out the very next day , beautifully 
  shave , frock coat fit like a glove , brand new eye - glass , 
  etc . , etc . I go and walk in the park with he , where I meet 
  some people I know , and at once tell they the story of his 
  " beautiful white leg . " 

  he be furious , especially as some ill - natured person have print 
  it in a Society paper . 

  to come to business , good and I take the diamond to Streeter 's to 
  be value , as we arrange , and really I be afraid to tell you what 
  they put they at , it seem so enormous . they say that of course it 
  be more or less guess - work , as such stone have never to their 
  knowledge be put on the market in anything like such quantity . 
  it appear that   with the exception of one or two of the large 
  they be of the fine water , and equal in every way to the good 
  brazilian stone . I ask they if they would buy they , but they 
  say that it be beyond their power to do so , and recommend we 
  to sell by degree , over a period of year indeed , for fear lest 
  we should flood the market . they offer , however , a hundred and 
  eighty thousand for a very small portion of they . 

  you must come home , Quatermain , and see about these thing , 
  especially if you insist upon make the magnificent present of 
  the third share , which do not belong to I , to my brother 
  George . as for Good , he be no good . his time be too much 
  occupy in shaving , and other matter connect with the vain 
  adorning of the body . but I think he be still down on his luck 
  about Foulata . he tell I that since he have be home he have not 
  see a woman to touch she , either as regard her figure or the 
  sweetness of her expression . 

  I want you to come home , my dear old comrade , and to buy a house 
  near here . you have do your day 's work , and have lot of money 
  now , and there be a place for sale quite close which would suit 
  you admirably . do come ; the soon the well ; you can finish 
  write the story of our adventure on board ship . we have refuse 
  to tell the tale till it be write by you , for fear lest we shall 
  not be believe . if you start on receipt of this you will reach 
  here by Christmas , and I book you to stay with I for that . good 
  be come , and George ; and so , by the way , be your boy Harry 
   there be a bribe for you . I have have he down for a week 's 
  shooting , and like he . he be a cool young hand ; he shoot I in the 
  leg , cut out the pellet , and then remark upon the advantage of 
  have a medical student with every shoot party ! 

  good - bye , old boy ; I can not   say any more , but I know that you will 
  come , if it be only to oblige 

  your sincere friend , 
  Henry Curtis . 

  P.S. - the tusk of the great bull that kill poor Khiva have now 
  be put up in the hall here , over the pair of buffalo horn you 
  give I , and look magnificent ; and the axe with which I chop 
  off Twala 's head be fix above my writing - table . I wish that we 
  could have manage to bring away the coat of chain armour . do not 
  lose poor Foulata 's basket in which you bring away the diamond . 

  H.C. 

 to - day be Tuesday . there be a steamer go on Friday , and I really 
 think that I must take Curtis at his word , and sail by she for England ,
